    <div class="introductory section" id="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>
      This specification defines a model for synchronization and timing of
      changes to the presentation of a Web page.
      This specification also defines an application programming interface for
      interacting with this model and it is expected that further specifications
      will define declarative means for exposing these features.
    </p></div><div id="sotd" class="introductory section"><h2>Status of This Document</h2><p><em>This section describes the status of this document at the time of its publication. Other documents may supersede this document. class="tocxref" href="#implementation-requirements"><span class="secno">9. </span>Implementation requirements</a><ul class="toc"><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#precision"><span class="secno">9.1 </span>Precision</a></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#conformance-criteria"><span class="secno">9.2 </span>Conformance criteria</a></li></ul></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#webidl-ref"><span class="secno">A. </span>Interface summary</a></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#algorithms-for-path-animation-effects"><span class="secno">B. </span>Algorithms for path animation effects</a></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#algorithms-for-event-dispatch"><span class="secno">C. </span>Algorithms for event dispatch</a><ul class="toc"><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#interval-boundaries-and-time-marks"><span class="secno">C.1 </span>Interval boundaries and time marks</a></li><li class="tocxref" href="#acknowledgements"><span class="secno">D. </span>Acknowledgements</a></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#references"><span class="secno">E. </span>References</a><ul class="toc"><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#normative-references"><span class="secno">E.1 </span>Normative references</a></li><li class="tocline"><a class="tocxref" href="#informative-references"><span class="secno">E.2 </span>Informative references</a></li></ul></li></ul></div>

    <div id="introduction" class="informative section">
      <!--OddPage--><h2><span class="secno">1. </span>Introduction</h2><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
      <p>
        Web Animations defines a model for supporting animation and
        synchronization on the Web platform.
        It is intended that other specifications will build on this model and
        expose its features through declarative means.
        In addition, this specification also defines a programming interface to
        the model that may be implemented by user agents that provide support
        for scripting.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="use-cases">
        <h3><span class="secno">1.1 </span>Use cases</h3>
        <p>
          The Web Animations model aims at two broad areas of application:
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt>User interface effects</dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Animation can be used to give visual clues and feedback to make
              a user interface more readily comprehensible.
            </p>
            <p>
              For example, a user action results in a table row being
              removed to represent an item being removed from a shopping cart.
              In such a case, fading the row to transparent and then shifting
              the subsequent rows up to fill the space over a few hundred
              milliseconds provides the user with clear feedback as to the
              results of their action as opposed to instantly removing the row
              from the DOM.
            </p>
            <p>
              To support this scenario not only are the animated effects of
              fading and shifting required, but so is synchronization, both
              between the animations, and between animations and scripted
              actions (removing the table row from the DOM after the animations
              have completed).
            </p>
          </dd>
          <dt>Storytelling and visualisation</dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Another type of animation uses the animated effect to convey
              a story or represent some information.
              Unlike user interface effects which are largely a presentational
              adjunct to the content, these animations form an essential part of
              the content presented to the user.
            </p>
            <p>
              For example, in an animated cartoon two cats fly through space
              to another planet leaving a rainbow trail behind them.
              After arriving at the planet a change of scene occurs and the user
              should decide whether or not the cats enter a magic mountain by
              selecting one of two preset destinations in the scene.
            </p>
            <p>
              This scenario requires the following features:
            </p>
            <ul>
              <li>animated effects for moving characters along a path as well as
                  warping a path (the rainbow trail),
              </li><li>synchronization that allows some actions to happen
                  simultaneously (the two cats moving) and others in sequence
                  (the change of scene),
              </li><li>play control to allow rewinding the cartoon, or changing its
                  playback rate to accommodate particular learning or
                  accessibility needs,
              </li><li>the ability to trigger animations in response to user input
            </li></ul>
            <p>
              Similar use cases in this category include visualising physical
              phenomena such as spring motion for educational purposes,
              or visualising data such as the prevalence of a disease over
              a geographical space over a year whereby animation is used to
              present the time-based component of the data.
            </p>
          </dd>
        </dl>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="relationship-to-other-specifications">
        <h3><span class="secno">1.2 </span>Relationship to other specifications</h3>
        <p>
          CSS Transitions [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>], CSS Animations 
          [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-ANIMATIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-ANIMATIONS</a></cite>], and SVG [<cite><a href="#bib-SVG112" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SVG112</a></cite>] all provide mechanisms that
          generate animated content on a Web page.
          Although the three specifications provide many similar features,
          they are described in different terms.
          This specification proposes an abstract animation model that
          encompasses the common features of all three specifications.
          This model is backwards-compatible with the current behavior of these
          specifications such that they can be defined in terms of this model
          without any observable change.
        </p>
        <p>
          The animation features in SVG 1.1 are defined in terms of SMIL
          Animation [<cite><a href="#bib-SMIL-ANIMATION" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SMIL-ANIMATION</a></cite>].
          It is intended that by defining SVG's animation features in terms of
          the Web Animations model, the dependency between SVG and SMIL
          Animation can be removed.
        </p>
        <p>
          The programming interface component of this specification makes
          some additions to interfaces defined in HTML5 [<cite><a href="#bib-HTML5" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">HTML5</a></cite>].
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="overview-of-this-specification">
        <h3><span class="secno">1.3 </span>Overview of this specification</h3>
        <p>
          This specification begins by defining an abstract model for animation.
          This is followed by a programming interface defined in terms of the
          abstract model.
          The programming interface is defined in terms of the abstract model
          and is only relevant to user agents that provide scripting support.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div></div>

    <div id="web-animations-model-overview" class="informative section">
      <!--OddPage--><h2><span class="secno">2. </span>Web Animations model overview</h2><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
      <p>
        At a glance, the Web Animations model consists of two largely
        independent pieces, a <em>timing model</em> and an <em>animation
        model</em>.  The role of these pieces is as follows:
      </p>
      <dl>
        <dt>Timing model</dt>
        <dd>
          Takes a moment in time and converts it to a proportional distance
          within a single iteration of an animation called the <em>time
          fraction</em>.
          An <em>iteration index</em> is also generated for animations
          that vary as they repeat.
        </dd>
        <dt>Animation model</dt>
        <dd>
          Takes the <em>time fractions</em> and <em>iteration indices</em>
          produced by the timing model and converts them into a series of values
          to apply to the target properties and attributes.
        </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
        Graphically, this flow can be represented as follows:
      </p>
      <div class="figure">
        <img src="img/timing-and-animation-models.svg" alt="Overview of the operation of the Web Animations model." width="600">
      </div>
      <p class="caption">
        Overview of the operation of the Web Animations model.<br>
        The current time is input to the timing model which produces a time
        fraction and an iteration index.<br>
        These parameters are used as input to the animation model which produces
        the values to apply.<br>
      </p>
      <p>
        For example, consider an animation that:
      </p>
      <ul>
        <li>starts after 3 seconds,</li>
        <li>runs twice,</li>
        <li>takes 2 seconds every time, and</li>
        <li>changes the width of a rectangle from 50 pixels to 100
            pixels.</li>
      </ul>
      <p>
        The first three points apply to the timing model.
        At a time of 6 seconds, it will calculate that the animation should be
        half-way through its second iteration and produces the result 0.5.
        The animation model then uses that information to calculate a width
        for the rectangle of 75.
      </p>
      <p>
        This specification begins with the timing model and then proceeds to
        the animation model.
      </p>
    </div></div>

    <div class="section" id="timing-model">
      <!--OddPage--><h2><span class="secno">3. </span>Timing model</h2>
      <p>
        This section describes and defines the behavior of the Web Animations
        timing model.
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">Timing events</a>, however, which are also a feature of the timing
        model, are described separately in <a href="#timing-events" class="sectionRef">section 5. Timing events</a>.
      </p>
    <div id="the-timing-model-at-a-glance" class="informative section">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.1 </span>The timing model at a glance</h3><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
      <p>
        Two features characterise the Web Animations timing model: it is
        <em>stateless</em> and it is <em>hierarchical</em>.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="stateless">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.1.1 </span>Stateless</h4>
        <p>
          The Web Animations timing model operates by taking an input time and
          producing an output time fraction.
          Since the output is based solely on the input time and is independent
          of previous inputs, the model may be described as stateless.
          This gives the model the following properties:
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt>Frame-rate independent</dt>
          <dd>
            Since the output is independent of previous inputs, the rate at
            which the model is sampled will not affect its progress.
            Provided the input times are proportional to the progress of
            real-world time, animations will progress at an identical rate
            regardless of the capabilities of the device running them.
          </dd>
          <dt>Direction-agnostic</dt>
          <dd>
            Since the sequence of inputs is insignificant, the model is
            directionless.
            This means that the model can be sampled in reverse or even in
            a backwards and forwards pattern without requiring any specialized
            handling.
          </dd>
          <dt>Constant-time seeking</dt>
          <dd>
            Since each input is independent of the previous input, the
            processing required to perform a seek operation, even far into the
            future, is at least potentially constant.
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p>
          There are a few apparent exceptions to the stateless behavior of the
          timing model.
        </p>
        <p>
          Firstly, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing events</a> are fired when, for example, one sample
          falls on the opposite side of an animation's interval boundary to the
          previous sample.
          This is certainly stative behavior.
          However, events should be considered as a layer added on top of the
          core timing model.
          When no event listeners are registered, the model is stateless.
        </p>
        <p>
          The other exception to this stateless behavior is that a number of
          methods defined in the <a href="#script-interface">programming
          interface</a> to the model provide play control such as pausing
          an item.
          These methods are defined in terms of the time at which they are
          called and are therefore stative.
          These methods are provided primarily for convenience and are not part
          of the core timing model but, like events, are layered on top.
        </p>
        <p>
          Finally, each time the model is sampled, it can be considered to
          establish a temporary state.
          While this temporary state affects the values returned from the <a href="#script-interface">programming interface</a>, it has no
          influence on the subsequent samples and hence does not conflict with
          the stateless qualities described above.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="hierarchical">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.1.2 </span>Hierarchical</h4>
        <p>
          The other characteristic feature of the Web Animations timing model is
          that time is inherited.
          Time begins with a monotonically increasing time source and cascades
          down a number of steps to each animation.
          At each step, time may be shifted backwards and forwards, scaled,
          reversed, paused, and repeated.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/time-hierarchy.svg" alt="A hierarchy of timing nodes" width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          A hierarchy of timing nodes.
          Each node in the tree derives its time from its parent node.
          At the root of the tree is the global clock.
        </p>
        <p>
          A consequence of this hierarchical arrangement is that complex
          animation arrangements can be reversed, scheduled, accelerated and so
          on as a whole unit since the manipulations applied to the parent
          cascade down to its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-descendant">descendants</a>.
          Furthermore, since time has a common source, it is easy to synchronize
          animations.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div></div>

    <div class="section" id="timing-model-concepts">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.2 </span>Timing model concepts</h3>
      <p>
        In Web Animations timing is based on a hierarchy of time relationships
        between timing nodes.
        Parent nodes provide timing information to their child nodes in the form
        of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a>.
        A <dfn id="dfn-time-value">time value</dfn> is a real number which nominally represents
        a number of seconds from some moment.
        The connection between <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> and wall-clock seconds may be
        obscured by any number of transformations applied to the value as it
        passes through the time hierarchy.
      </p>
      <p class="annotation">
        In the future we may have timelines that are based on UI gestures in
        which case the connection between time values and seconds will be
        weakened even further.
      </p>
      <p>
        Periodically, the user agent will trigger an update to the timing model
        in a process called <dfn id="dfn-sampling">sampling</dfn>.
        On each <dfn id="dfn-sample">sample</dfn> the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> of each timing node are
        updated.
      </p>
      <p class="note">
        A more precise definition of when the model is updated when scripting is
        involved is provided in <a href="#script-execution-and-live-updates-to-the-model" class="sectionRef">section 6.24 Script execution and live updates to the model</a>.
      </p>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="the-global-clock">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.3 </span>The global clock</h3>
      <p>
        At the root of the Web Animations timing hierarchy is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global
        clock</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The <dfn id="dfn-global-clock">global clock</dfn> is a source of monotonically increasing
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> unaffected by adjustments to the system clock.
        The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> produced by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> represent
        wall-clock seconds from an unspecified historical moment.
        The absolute value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> produced by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global
        clock</a> are insignificant, only their rate of change.
      </p>
      <p class="note">
        Note that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> is not exposed in the <a href="#script-interface">programming interface</a> and nor is it
        expected to be exposed by markup.
        As a result the moment from which <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a>
        are measured, that is, the zero time of the clock, is allowed to be
        implementation-dependent.
        One user agent may measure the number of seconds since the the user
        agent was loaded whilst another may use the time when the device was
        started.
        Both approaches are acceptable and produce no observable difference
        in the output of the model.
      </p>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="timelines">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.4 </span>Timelines</h3>
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-timeline">timeline</dfn> provides a source of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> for the
        purpose of synchronization.
      </p>
      <p>
        Typically, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is tied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> such
        that its absolute time is calculated as a fixed offset from the time of
        the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a>.
        This offset is established by designating some moment as the timeline's
        <dfn id="dfn-zero-time">zero time</dfn> and recording the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> at that moment.
        At subsequent moments, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the timeline is
        calculated as the difference between the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of
        the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> and the value recorded at the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-zero-time">zero time</a>.
      </p>
      <p class="annotation">
        Note that we anticipate that other types of timelines may be introduced
        in the future that are not tied to the global clock.
        For example, a timeline whose time values correspond to UI gestures.
      </p>
      <p>
        Since a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> may be defined to relative a moment that has yet
        to occur, it may not always be able to return a meaningful <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time
        value</a>.
        A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is considered to be <dfn id="dfn-not-started">not started</dfn> when it is
        in such a state that it cannot produce a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a>.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="the-document-timeline">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.4.1 </span>The document timeline</h4>
        <p>
          Each document has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> called the <dfn id="dfn-document-timeline">document
          timeline</dfn> whose <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> at a given moment is calculated
          as a fixed offset from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a> such that its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-zero-time">zero
          time</a> corresponds to the moment immediately prior to dispatching
          the load event of the document.
          Prior to this moment, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-document-timeline">document timeline</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-not-started">not
          started</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          For documents that support the concept of <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/html51/dom.html#current-document-readiness
          ">current document readiness</a>, this is the moment after the <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/html51/dom.html#current-document-readiness
          ">current document readiness</a> has changed to "complete" but
          before dispatching the load event.
          For user agents that support Navigation Timing [<cite><a href="#bib-NAVIGATION-TIMING" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">NAVIGATION-TIMING</a></cite>],
          this occurs between the <em>domComplete</em> and
          <em>loadEventStart</em> timings.
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          This is not correct.
          We need a means to start animations prior to document load.
        </div>
        <p>
          Since the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-document-timeline">document timeline</a> is tied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-global-clock">global clock</a>
          by a fixed offset, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> reported by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-document-timeline">document
          timeline</a> increase monotonically.
          Furthermore, since no scaling is applied, these <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a>
          are proportional to wall-clock seconds.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="players">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.5 </span>Players</h3>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          The children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> are called <em>players</em>.
          A player takes a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> which is a static description of
          some timed behavior and binds it to a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> so that it runs.
          A player also allows run-time control of the connection between the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> and its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> by providing pausing,
          seeking, and speed control.
          The relationship between a player and a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is analogous
          to that of a DVD player and a DVD.
        </p>
      </div>
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-player">player</dfn> connects a single <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>, called its
        <dfn id="dfn-source-content">source content</dfn>, to a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> and provides playback
        control.
      </p>
      <p>
        A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> records the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>
        at which its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> is scheduled to begin
        as the <dfn id="dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        When a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is created, it is assigned a globally unique
        sequence number called the <dfn id="dfn-player-sequence-number">player sequence number</dfn>.
        This number is used to resolve the sort order of players that have the
        same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a> for a variety of
        situations such as combining animations, queuing events, and returning
        the list of players.
      </p>
      <p class="annotation">
        If we later allow restarting a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> (e.g. by adding
        a <code>play()</code> method), we might update the sequence number at
        this point and rename it to something more appropriate.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="the-current-time-of-a-player">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.5.1 </span>The current time of a player</h4>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">Players</a> provide a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> to their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source
          content</a> called the player's <dfn id="dfn-current-time">current time</dfn>.
          The calculation of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> is as follows:
        </p>
        <blockquote>
          <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> =
          (<var>timeline time</var> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start
          time</a>) * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a>
          - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a></code>
        </blockquote>
        <p>
          Where:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li><var>timeline time</var> is the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> with which this <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is associated.</li>
          <li><var>start time</var> is the player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>.</li>
          <li><var>playback rate</var> is the player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> value described in <a href="#speed-control" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.3 Speed control</a>.</li>
          <li><var>time drift</var> is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> value described in
          <a href="#seeking-and-pausing" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2 Seeking and pausing</a>.</li>
        </ul>
        <p>
          If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> with which is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is associated is
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-not-started">not started</a> then the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> is <code>null</code>.
        </p>
        <p>
          It is often useful to treat the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> as zero when it
          would otherwise be <code>null</code>.
          We define the <dfn id="dfn-effective-current-time">effective current time</dfn> as being equal
          to <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> unless the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> is
          <code>null</code>,
          in which case the <var>effective current time</var> is zero.
        </p>
        <p>
          The procedure for performing manual updates to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a>
          is defined in <a href="#performing-a-seek" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2.6 Performing a seek</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="seeking-and-pausing">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.5.2 </span>Seeking and pausing</h4>
        <p>
          Seeking and pausing a player are closely related and are described
          here together.
        </p>
        <div id="introduction-to-seeking" class="informative section">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.1 </span>Introduction to seeking</h5><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
          <p>
            Changing the current playback position of a player can be used to
            rewind its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> to its start point, fast-forward
            to a point in the future, or to provide ad-hoc synchronization
            between timed items.
          </p>
          <p>
            However, in Web Animations, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start
            time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> has special significance in determining
            the priority of animations (see <a href="#combining-animations" class="sectionRef">section 4.2 Combining animations</a>) and so we cannot simply adjust the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>.
            Instead, an additional offset is introduced called the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time
            drift</a> that further offsets a player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> from
            its timeline.
            The effect of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> when seeking is illustrated
            below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/seeking.svg" alt="The effect of seeking a player." width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            At time <var>t</var>, a seek is performed on the player changing its
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> from 1.5s to 2s.<br>
            As a result, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> is set to -0.5s.<br>
            Note that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a> indicated
            by a red star does not change.
          </p>
          <p>
            It is possible to seek a player even if its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-not-started">not started</a>.
            Once the timeline begins, the player will begin playback from the
            seeked time.
          </p>
        </div></div>
        <div id="introduction-to-pausing" class="informative section">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.2 </span>Introduction to pausing</h5><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
          <p>
            Pausing can be used to temporarily suspend a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
            Like seeking, pausing effectively causes the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> of
            a player to be offset from its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> by means of
            setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            The effect of pausing on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> is
            illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/pausing.svg" alt="The effect of pausing a player." width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            The effect of pausing a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.<br>
            Whether pausing before or after a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>
            the duration of the interval during which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> was
            paused is added to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> whilst the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a> remains unaffected.
          </p>
        </div></div>
        <div class="section" id="seeking-and-pausing-properties">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.3 </span>Seeking and pausing properties</h5>
          <p>
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">Players</a> track three properties related to seeking and
            pausing.
          </p>
          <dl>
            <dt><dfn id="dfn-time-drift">time drift</dfn></dt>
            <dd>
              The offset from a player's scheduled current time as defined by
              its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>, and its actual
              current time after accounting for the effects of seeking and
              pausing.
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> is initially zero and is updated as per the
              definition in <a href="#calculating-the-time-drift" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2.4 Calculating the time drift</a>.
            </dd>
            <dt><dfn id="dfn-paused-state">paused state</dfn></dt>
            <dd>
              A boolean value that is true if the player is currently paused.
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is initially false.
            </dd>
            <dt><dfn id="dfn-pause-start-time">pause start time</dfn></dt>
            <dd>
              The player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-effective-current-time">effective current time</a> at the time when the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> was last newly true.
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-pause-start-time">pause start time</a> is initially zero.
            </dd>
          </dl>
          <p>
            A number of calculations for performing seeking and pausing are
            defined to operate even when the associated <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-not-started">not started</a>.
            For such situations we define the <dfn id="dfn-effective-timeline-time">effective timeline time</dfn>
            as the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> associated
            with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>;
            if the timeline is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-not-started">not started</a>, then the <var>effective
            timeline time</var> is zero.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="calculating-the-time-drift">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.4 </span>Calculating the time drift</h5>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> value is both a stored and a calculated value.
            When a player is paused, the value is calculated from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-pause-start-time">pause
            start time</a>.
            When a player is not paused, the stored value is used.
            The stored value is initially zero, and is updated when the player
            is unpaused or seeked.
          </p>
          <p>
            The value of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> at a given moment is calculated as
            follows:
          </p>
          <dl class="switch">
            <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is true,</dt>
            <dd>
              Return the result of 
              <code>(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-effective-timeline-time">effective timeline time</a> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>) * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> -
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-pause-start-time">pause start time</a></code>.
            </dd>
            <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
            <dd>
              Return the stored value for this property.
            </dd>
          </dl>
          <p class="todo">
            These formulae need to be verified since removing the special
            behavior regarding pausing before the start time.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="updating-the-paused-state">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.5 </span>Updating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a></h5>
          <p>
            The procedure for updating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is as
            follows:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
              Let <var>new value</var> be the new paused state to set.
            </li>
            <li>
              If <var>new value</var> equals the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a>,
              return.
            </li>
            <li>
              The next step depends on the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> as
              follows,
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is true,</dt>
                <dd>
                  Set the <em>stored</em> value of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> to the
                  <em>current calculated</em> value of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> as
                  defined in <a href="#calculating-the-time-drift" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2.4 Calculating the time drift</a>.
                </dd>
                <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
                <dd>
                  Record the current value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-effective-current-time">effective current time</a>
                  as <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-pause-start-time">pause start time</a>.
                </dd>
              </dl>
            </li>
            <li>
              Update <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> to <var>new value</var>.
            </li>
          </ol>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="performing-a-seek">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.2.6 </span>Performing a seek</h5>
          <p>
            <dfn id="dfn-seeking">Seeking</dfn> is the process of updating a player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current
            time</a> to a desired value.
            It is achieved using the following procedure:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>Let <var>seek time</var> be the desired <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> for
                the player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a>.</li>
            <li>The steps for adjusting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> depend on the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> as follows:
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is true,</dt>
                <dd>
                  Set <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-pause-start-time">pause start time</a> to <var>seek time</var>.
                </dd>
                <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a> is false,</dt>
                <dd>
                  Set the stored value for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a> to
                  the result of evaluating
                  <code>(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-effective-timeline-time">effective timeline time</a> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a>)
                     * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> -
                     <var>seek time</var></code>.
                </dd>
              </dl>
            </li>
          </ol>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing events</a> queued when a seek is performed are
            described in <a href="#event-dispatch-and-seeking-a-player" class="sectionRef">section 5.7.2 Event dispatch and seeking a player</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="speed-control">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.5.3 </span>Speed control</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            The rate of play of a player can be controlled by setting its
            <em>playback rate</em>.
            For example, setting a playback rate of 2 will cause the player's
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> to increase at twice the rate of its
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>.
            Similarly, a playback rate of -1 will cause the player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current
            time</a> to decrease at the same rate as the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> from
            its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> increase.
          </p>
          <p>
            Note that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> also have a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> associated with
            them that behaves differently to that defined here.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">Players</a> have a <dfn id="dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback
          rate">playback rate</dfn> that provides a scaling factor from the rate
          of change of the associated <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> to
          the player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a>.
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> is initially 1.
        </p>
        <p>
          Setting a player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a>
          to zero effectively pauses the player but without affecting the
          player's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paused-state">paused state</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="updating-the-playback-rate">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.5.3.1 </span>Updating the playback rate</h5>
          <p>
            Changes to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a>
            also trigger a compensatory seek so that that the player's
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> is unaffected by the change to the playback
            rate.
          </p>
          <p>
            The procedure is as follows:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>Let <var>previous time</var> be the value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-effective-current-time">effective
                current time</a> before updating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a>.</li>
            <li>Update the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> to
                the new value.</li>
            <li>Seek to <var>previous time</var> using the procedure defined in
                <a href="#performing-a-seek" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2.6 Performing a seek</a>.</li>
          </ol>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="timed-items">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.6 </span>Timed items</h3>
      <p>
        The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>, if set, is a type of
        <dfn id="dfn-timed-item">timed item</dfn>.
        There are two types of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>:
      </p>
      <ul>
        <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a>, and</li>
        <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a>.</li>
      </ul>
      <p>
        At a given moment, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> can be associated with at most
        one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> can be chained together into a hierarchy using
        <a>timings groups</a>.
        Only the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-root">root</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> of such a hierarchy can be <dfn id="dfn-directly-associated-with-a-player" title="directly associated with a player">directly associated</dfn> with
        a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
        Attempting to associate a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> that has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing
        group</a> with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> results in the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> being
        removed from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> first.
        A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> with an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> that is
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directly-associated-with-a-player">directly associated with a player</a> is <dfn id="dfn-indirectly-associated-with-a-player" title="indirectly associated with a player">indirectly associated</dfn>
        with that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>, <var>item</var>, is <dfn id="dfn-associated-with-a-timeline">associated with
        a timeline</dfn>, <var>timeline</var>, if <var>item</var> is
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directly-associated-with-a-player" title="directly associated with a player">directly</a> or
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-indirectly-associated-with-a-player" title="indirectly associated with a player">indirectly</a> associated
        with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> which, in turn, is associated with
        <var>timeline</var>.
      </p>
      <p>
        All types of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> define a number of common properties
        which are described in the following sections.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="the-active-interval">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.6.1 </span>The active interval</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            The period that a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is scheduled to run is called
            its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
            Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> has only one such interval.
          </p>
          <p>
            The lower bound of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is determined by the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
            item</a> but may be shifted by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
            item</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            The upper bound of the interval is determined by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            The relationship between the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start
            time</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>, and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> is
            illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/active-interval-examples.svg" alt="Examples of the effect of the start delay on the endpoints
                    of the active interval" width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            Examples of the effect of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> on the endpoints of
            the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.<br>
            (a) A timed item with no delay; the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> and beginning of the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> are coincident.<br>
            (b) A timed item with a positive delay; the beginning of the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is deferred by the delay.<br>
            (c) A timed item with a negative delay; the beginning of the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is brought forward by the delay.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> define an <dfn id="dfn-active-interval">active interval</dfn> which is the
          period of time during which the item is scheduled to produce its
          effect with the exception of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill modes</a> which apply outside
          the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The lower bound of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is defined by the
          combination of the timed item's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start
          time</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>
        </p>
        <p>
          A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <dfn id="dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start
          time</dfn> is the moment at which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a>, if
          any, has scheduled the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> to begin.
          It is expressed in <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a>.
          In most cases, including the case when the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> has no
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start
          time</a> is zero.
          The singular exception is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing groups</a> which set the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start times</a> of their children as
          described in <a href="#the-start-time-of-children-of-a-sequence-timing-group" class="sectionRef">section 3.13.4.1 The start time of children of a sequence timing group</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          In addition to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a>,
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> also has a <dfn id="dfn-start-delay">start delay</dfn> which is an
          offset from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a>.
          Unlike the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> which is
          determined by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>
          is a property of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> itself.
        </p>
        <p>
          The lower bound of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a><a> of a </a><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>,
          expressed in <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time" title="inherited time">inherited time space</a>, is
          the sum of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> and the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          These definitions are incorporated in the calculation of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local
          time</a> (see <a href="#local-time-and-inherited-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.6.2 Local time and inherited time</a>) and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The length of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is called the <dfn id="dfn-active-duration">active
          duration</dfn>, the calculation of which is defined in <a href="#calculating-the-active-duration" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.2 Calculating the active duration</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="local-time-and-inherited-time">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.6.2 </span>Local time and inherited time</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            In Web Animations all times are relative to some point of reference.
            These different points of reference produce different <em>time
            spaces</em>.
          </p>
          <p>
            This can be compared to coordinate spaces as used in computer
            graphics.
            The zero time of a time space is analogous to the origin of
            a coordinate space.
          </p>
          <p>
            Just as with coordinate spaces, time spaces can also be nested.
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">Timing groups</a> typically perform some
            transformations on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a> they
            receive from their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group" title="parent timing group">parent</a> or
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> before passing on the transformed <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time values</a>
            to their children.
            Child <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> then operate <em>within</em> that
            transformed time space.
          </p>
          <p>
            Children take the transformed time values from their
            parent&#x2014;called the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a>&#x2014; and add their
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> to establish their
            own <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time" title="local time">local time space</a> as illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/local-time.svg" alt="Inherited time and local time." width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            Inherited time and local time.<br>
            At time <var>t</var>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> is 2.5.<br>
            For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> (a) which has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of 1, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local
              time</a> is 1.5.<br>
            For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> (b) which has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of 1
              and a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> of 1,
              the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is also 1.5
              since <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is based on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> only,
              and not on its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          For a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>, the <dfn id="dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</dfn> at
          a given moment is based on the first matching condition from the
          following:
        </p>
        <dl class="switch">
          <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a>,</dt>
          <dd>
            the inherited time is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a>'s current
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time" title="transformed time">transformed time value</a>.
          </dd>
          <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is directly associated with
              a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>,</dt>
          <dd>
            the inherited time is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> of the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
          </dd>
          <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
          <dd>
            the inherited time is <code>null</code>.
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-local-time">local time</dfn> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> minus its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a>.
          If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> is <code>null</code> then the local time
          is also <code>null</code>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="timed-item-states">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.6.3 </span>Timed item states</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            At given moment, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> may be described as being in
            one of several overlapping states.
            These states are only established for the duration of a single
            sample and are primarily a convenience for describing stative parts
            of the model such as event dispatch.
          </p>
          <p>
            The different states are illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/timed-item-states.svg" alt="An example of the different states used for describing a
                    timed item." width="700">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            An example of the different states used for describing a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
            item</a> at a given time.
            Note that a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is considered to be <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a>
            for all times inside the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> as well as times
            outside the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> where a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> is
            applied.
          </p>
          <p>
            These states and their useage within the model are summarised as
            follows:
          </p>
          <dl>
            <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scheduled">scheduled</a></dt>
            <dd>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> falls before the item's
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
              This state is only used in conjunction with the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active"><em>active</em></a> state to define the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current"><em>current</em></a>
              state.
            </dd>
            <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a></dt>
            <dd>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> falls inside the item's
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
              Transitions to and from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active"><em>active</em></a> state trigger
              timing events as defined in <a href="#timing-events" class="sectionRef">section 5. Timing events</a>.
            </dd>
            <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current">current</a></dt>
            <dd>
              <p>
                The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> falls either before or
                inside the item's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, <em>or</em> the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>
                falls before or inside its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> thereby
                opening up the possibility that this <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> might
                play again (e.g. due to repeating).
              </p>
              <p>
                This state is used in the <a href="#script-interface">programming interface</a> to identify
                all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">players</a> that are likely to be
                of interest.
              </p>
              <p>
                Furthermore, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current">current</a> state provides an important
                definition for managing the amount of memory required by
                implementations.
                Assuming a monotonically increasing <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>, in the
                absence of dynamic changes to the model, an implementation can
                safely discard all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> that are <em>not</em>
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current">current</a> and not referenced elsewhere provided they take
                care to preserve any <a>fill values</a> since they will not have
                any dynamic effect.
              </p>
            </dd>
            <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a></dt>
            <dd>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> falls either inside the
              item's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> or outside the interval but at
              a time where the item's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> (see <a href="#fill-behavior" class="sectionRef">section 3.7 Fill behavior</a>) causes it to affect
              its target.
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> only produce a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> when the
              item is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a>.
              At all other times, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
              item</a> is <code>null</code>.
            </dd>
          </dl>
          <p>
            The normative definition of each of these states follows.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is <dfn id="dfn-scheduled">scheduled</dfn> if <em>either</em> of the
          following conditions is true:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>the timed item's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is not <code>null</code> and is
              less than the item's <code>startDelay</code>, or</li>
          <li>the timed item has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> which is
              a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scheduled">scheduled</a> timed item.</li>
        </ol>
        <p>
          A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is <dfn id="dfn-active">active</dfn> if <em>all</em> of the
          following conditions are met:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is not
              <code>null</code>, and</li>
          <li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is <em>greater than or
              equal</em> to its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>, and</li>
          <li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is <em>less than</em>
              the sum of its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>.</li>
        </ol>
        <p>
          A timed item is <dfn id="dfn-current">current</dfn> if it is either <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scheduled">scheduled</a> or
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a> or it has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> and the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current">current</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          A timed item is <dfn id="dfn-in-effect">in effect</dfn> if its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> as
          calculated according to the procedure in <a href="#calculating-the-active-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.3.1 Calculating the active time</a> is not
          <code>null</code>.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="fill-behavior">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.7 </span>Fill behavior</h3>
      <p>
        The effect of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> outside its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is
        determined by its <dfn id="dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The possible <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill modes</a> are:
      </p>
      <ul>
        <li>none,</li>
        <li>forwards,</li>
        <li>backwards, and</li>
        <li>both.</li>
      </ul>
      <p>
        The normative definition of these modes is incorporated in the
        calculation of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> in <a href="#calculating-the-active-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.3.1 Calculating the active time</a>.
      </p>
      <div id="fill-modes" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.7.1 </span>Fill modes</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          The effect of each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> is as follows:
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt>none</dt>
          <dd>
            The timed item has no effect outside of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          </dd>
          <dt>forwards</dt>
          <dd>
            For times that occur later than the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the
            timed item will continue to produce the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time" title="transformed time">transformed time value</a> that was used at
            the end of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.

            For times that occur before the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the
            timed item will have no effect.
          </dd>
          <dt>backwards</dt>
          <dd>
            For times that occur before the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the timed
            item will produce the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time" title="transformed time">transformed
            time value</a> that will be used at the start of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active
            interval</a>.

            For times that occur later than the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the
            timed item will have no effect.
          </dd>
          <dt>both</dt>
          <dd>
            For times that occur before the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the
            <span class="prop-value">backwards</span> fill behavior is used.

            For times that occur after the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, the
            <span class="prop-value">forwards</span> fill behavior is used.
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p>
          Some examples of the these fill modes are illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/animation-state-and-fill-behavior.svg" alt="Examples of various fill modes and the states produced." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Examples of various fill modes and the states produced.<br>
          (a) fill mode &#x2018;none&#x2019;. The timed item has no effect outside
              its active interval.<br>
          (b) fill mode &#x2018;forwards&#x2019;. After the active interval has
              finished, the timed value continues to maintain a fill value.<br>
          (c) fill mode &#x2018;backwards&#x2019;. The timed item produces a fill
              value until the start of the active interval.<br>
          (d) fill mode &#x2018;both&#x2019;. Both before and after the active
              interval the timed item produces a fill value.
        </p> 
        <p class="note">
          Note that setting a fill mode has no bearing on the endpoints of the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          However, the fill mode <em>does</em> have an effect on various other
          properties of the timing model since the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> of a timed
          item is only defined (that is, not <code>null</code>) inside the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> <em>or</em> when a fill is applied.
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            As currently defined, when filling, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> uses an
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> equal to either zero or its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a>, and this is used as the basis for the time which is
            inherited by its children.
          </p>
          <p>
            This has the effect of &#x2018;snapshotting&#x2019; the children for
            the duration of the parent's fill.
            As a result, if a child is active at the boundary of an ancestor's
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> and that ancestor is configured to fill at
            the point, the child will remain active through the ancestor's fill
            even if the child is <em>not</em> configured to fill in the given
            direction.
          </p>
          <p>
            This behavior may be surprising in some circumstances..
            It is particularly noticeable in the case of an ancestor with
            backwards fill, as for the common case where children are aligned at
            the start of the parent's active interval, they will also fill
            backwards regardless of their fill mode.
          </p>
          <p>
            In order to provide control of this behavior we
            are considering modifying the definition of fill to depend on the
            parent's fill state.
            In particular, when a parent is filling, a child will only be active
            (and its descendants thus have an effect) if it too is configured to
            fill in that direction.
          </p>
          <p>
            In order to provide the currently-defined behavior (which we expect
            is useful for many situations), we would likely introduce a new
            'auto' fill mode, which means that a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s fill mode
            should match that of its parent, if present, or use forward fill
            otherwise.
          </p>
          <p>
            See <a href="http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/public-fx/2013AprJun/0184.html">section
            2 (Fill modes on descendants) of minuted discussion from Tokyo 2013
              F2F</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            Currently <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a> that generate results outside the
            range [0, 1] will behave unexpectedly when applied to animation
            groups, as children will increase iterations or enter into fill mode
            rather than continuing to extrapolate along their defined behaviours
            (which is what they would do if the timing function applied to them
            directly).
          </p>
          <p>
            To fix this it is possible we will wish to introduce 'overflow' fill
            modes that respond to time values larger than or smaller than the
            active time range by extrapolating rather than filling.
          </p>
          <p>
            See <a href="http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/public-fx/2013AprJun/0184.html">section
            15 (Overflowing fill) of minuted discussion from Tokyo 2013 F2F</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div></div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="repeating">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.8 </span>Repeating</h3>
      <div class="section" id="iteration-intervals">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.8.1 </span>Iteration intervals</h4>
        <p>
          It is possible to specify that a timed item should repeat
          a fixed number of times or indefinitely.
          This repetition occurs <em>within</em> the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          The span of time during which a single repetition takes place is
          called an <dfn id="dfn-iteration-interval">iteration interval</dfn>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Unlike the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>, a timed item can have multiple
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-interval">iteration intervals</a> although typically only the interval
          corresponding to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> is of interest.
        </p>
        <p>
          The length of a single iteration is called the <dfn id="dfn-iteration-duration">iteration
          duration</dfn>.
          The initial <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> of a timed item is simply its
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
