          The <dfn id="dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</dfn> of a timed item is zero,
          however some specific types of timed item such as timing groups
          override this behavior and provide an alternative intrinsic duration
          (see <a href="#the-intrinsic-iteration-duration-of-a-parallel-timing-group" class="sectionRef">section 3.13.3.2 The intrinsic iteration duration of a parallel timing group</a> and <a href="#the-intrinsic-iteration-duration-of-a-sequence-timing-group" class="sectionRef">section 3.13.4.2 The intrinsic iteration duration of a sequence timing group</a>).
        </p>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> may be set by the
          author to represent a value other than the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration
          duration</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            Comparing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> and the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a> we have:
          </p>
          <dl>
            <dt>Iteration duration</dt>
            <dd>
              The time taken for a single iteration of the timed item to
              complete.
            </dd>
            <dt>Active duration</dt>
            <dd>
              The time taken for the entire timed item to complete, including
              repetitions.
              This may be longer or shorter than the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>.
            </dd>
          </dl>
          <p>
            The relationship between the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a> is illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/iteration-intervals.svg" alt="Comparison of the iteration duration and active time." width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            A comparison of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a> of a timed item with an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> of 2.5.
            Note that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> for the final iteration does
            not change, it is simply cut-off by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="controlling-iteration">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.8.2 </span>Controlling iteration</h4>
        <p>
          The number of times a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> repeats is called its
          <dfn id="dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</dfn>.
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> is a real number greater than or equal to
          zero.
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> may also be positive infinity to represent
          that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> repeats indefinitely.
        </p>
        <p>
          In addition to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> also
          have an <dfn id="dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</dfn> property which specifies an offset
          into the series of iterations at which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> should
          begin.
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> is a finite real number greater than or
          equal to zero.
        </p>
        <p>
          The behavior of these parameters is defined in the calculations in <a href="#core-timed-item-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 3.10 Core timed item calculations</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            The effect of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a>
            parameters is illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/iteration-count-and-start.svg" alt="The effect of the iteration count and iteration start
                    parameters" width="600">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            The effect of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a>
            parameters.<br>
            In the first case the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> is 2.5 resulting in the
            third iteration being cut-off half way through its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-interval">iteration
            interval</a>.<br>
            The second case is the same but with an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> of
            0.5.
            This causes the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> to begin half way through the
            first iteration.
          </p>
          <p>
            Unlike the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> parameter, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration
            start</a> parameter does not effect the length of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            Note that values of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> greater than or equal to
            one are generally not useful unless used in combination with an
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> that has an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation">accumulation operation</a>
            property of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation-sum" title="accumulation operation sum">sum</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="iteration-time-space" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.8.3 </span>Iteration time space</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          We have already encountered different time spaces in describing
          <a>local time and inherited time</a> (see <a href="#local-time-and-inherited-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.6.2 Local time and inherited time</a>).
          Repetition introduces yet another time space: the iteration time
          space.
        </p>
        <p>
          <em>Iteration time space</em> is a time space whose zero time is the
          beginning of a timed item's current iteration.
        </p>
        <p>
          Within the Web Animations model we also refer to <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active
          time</a> which is a time relative to the beginning of the active
          interval.
          This time space, however, is internal to the model and not exposed in
          the script interface or in markup.
        </p>
        <p>
          These time spaces are illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/time-spaces.svg" alt="A comparison of item time, active time, and iteration time." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          A comparison of item time, active time, and iteration time for an
          animation with a iteration duration of 1s and an iteration count of
          2.5.
        </p>
        <p class="note">
          Note that while the time spaces themselves are not bounded, Web
          Animations defines <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration
          time</a> such that they are clamped to a set range as shown in the
          diagram.
          For example, whilst a time of -1 second is a valid time in
          <em>active time space</em>, the procedure for calculating the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> defined in <a href="#calculating-the-active-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.3.1 Calculating the active time</a> will
          never return a negative value.
        </p>
        <p>
          In addition to these time spaces we can also refer to the
          <em>document time space</em> which is time space of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time
          values</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-document-timeline">document timeline</a> of the <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/html5/browsers.html#active-document">active
          document</a>.
        </p>
      </div></div>
      <div id="interval-timing" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.8.4 </span>Interval timing</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          When a timed item repeats we must define the behavior at the iteration
          boundaries.
          For this and indeed for all interval-timing, Web Animations uses an
          endpoint-exclusive timing model.
          This means that whilst the begin time of an interval
          is included in the interval, the end time time is not.
          In interval notation this can written <code>[begin,end)</code>.
          This model provides sensible behavior when intervals are repeated and
          sequenced since there is no overlap between the intervals.
        </p>
        <p>
          In the examples below, for the repeated item, at local time 1s,
          the iteration time is 0.
          For the sequenced items, at inherited time 1s, only item B will be
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a>; there is no overlap.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/endpoint-exclusive-timing.svg" alt="Illustration of end-point exclusive timing." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Illustration of end-point exclusive timing. For both repeated and
          sequenced timed items there is no overlap at the boundaries between
          intervals.
        </p>
        <p>
          An exception to this behavior is that when performing a <a href="#fill-behavior">fill</a>, if the fill begins at an
          interval endpoint, the endpoint is used.
          This behavior falls out of the algorithm given in <a href="#calculating-the-iteration-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.3.3 Calculating the iteration time</a> and is illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/endpoint-exclusive-timing-and-fill.svg" alt="Effect of iterations and fill on iteration time." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          After one iteration, the iteration time is 0, but after two iterations
          (and thereonwards), the iteration time is equal to the iteration
          duration due to the special behavior defined when a timed item fills.
        </p>
      </div></div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="timed-item-speed-control">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.9 </span>Timed item speed control</h3>
      <p>
        Like <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">players</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> also have a <dfn id="dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</dfn> parameter.
        The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
        item</a> is a finite real number that acts as a multiplier when
        calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> from its
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The effect of setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback
        rate</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> differs from the setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> on a player.
        Its behavior is defined in the timing calculations given in <a href="#core-timed-item-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 3.10 Core timed item calculations</a>.
      </p>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          In summary, the behavior of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback
          rate">playback rate</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is as follows:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> is applied
            only to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> and not to
            the time while it is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay" title="start delay">delayed</a> or <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode" title="fill mode">filling</a>.
          </li>
          <li>
            Setting a negative <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback
            rate</a> on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> causes the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> to
            begin at the end of its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
            This differs from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback
            rate</a> on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
            Setting a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> on
            a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> to a negative value at a moment before the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>'s source content has begun, will result in the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> never playing.
          </li>
          <li>
            Setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> of
            a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> affects the calculated value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
            duration</a> (see <a href="#calculating-the-active-duration" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.2 Calculating the active duration</a>).
          </li>
          <li>
            <p>
              Changing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
              of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> whose <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is within its
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> will cause it to jump.
              This is because the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> will be updated but the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> will not.
            </p>
            <p>
              Furthermore, if other <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> depend on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
              item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>, such as sibling <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
              items</a> in a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a>, they too may jump as
              a result of setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>.
            </p>
            <p>
              For runtime speed control the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> of the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> should be used.
            </p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="core-timed-item-calculations">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.10 </span>Core timed item calculations</h3>
      <div id="overview" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.10.1 </span>Overview</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          At the core of the Web Animations timing model is the process that
          takes an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> value and converts it to an
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Following this further transformations are applied before resulting at
          a final <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The first step in this process is to calculate the boundary when the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a>, that is, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
          duration</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          This process is illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/active-duration-calculation.svg" alt="Calculation of the active duration." width="650">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Calculation of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> is based on
          multiplying the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration
          count</a> and then dividing by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The process for calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> is normatively
          defined in <a href="#calculating-the-active-duration" class="sectionRef">section 3.10.2 Calculating the active duration</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Having established the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>, the process for
          transforming a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> into its
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> is illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/time-calculations.svg" alt="An overview of timing model calculations." width="650">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          An overview of timing model calculations.<br>
          (1) The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> is converted into a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> by
          incorporating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a>.<br>
          (2) The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is converted into an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> by
          incorporating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>.<br>
          (3) The <a>playback rate</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> properties are
          applied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> to produce the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active
          time</a>.<br>
          (4) The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> is then converted to an offset
          within a single iteration: the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a>.<br>
          (5) The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a> is converted into a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed time</a>
          by incorporating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-playback-direction">playback direction</a>.<br>
          (6) Finally, a timing function is applied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed
          time</a> to produce the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The first step, calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is described in <a href="#local-time-and-inherited-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.6.2 Local time and inherited time</a>.
          Steps 2 to 4 in the diagram are described in the following sections.
          Steps 5 and 6 are described in
          <a href="#calculating-the-directed-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.11.1 Calculating the directed time</a>
          and
          <a href="#calculating-the-transformed-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.12.6 Calculating the transformed time</a>
          respectively.
        </p>
      </div></div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-active-duration">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.10.2 </span>Calculating the active duration</h4>
        <p>
          In order to calculate the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> we first define the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-repeated-duration">repeated duration</a> as follows:
        </p>
        <blockquote>
          <dfn id="dfn-repeated-duration">repeated duration</dfn> =
            <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> *
                  <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a></code>
        </blockquote>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> is calculated according to the following
          steps:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> is
            zero, return <code>Infinity</code>.
          </li>
          <li>
            Otherwise, return <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-repeated-duration">repeated duration</a>
            / abs(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>)</code>.
          </li>
        </ol>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="transforming-the-local-time">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.10.3 </span>Transforming the local time</h4>
        <div class="section" id="calculating-the-active-time">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.10.3.1 </span>Calculating the active time</h5>
          <p>
            The <dfn id="dfn-active-time">active time</dfn> is based on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a>
            and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>.
            It is defined only when the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a>
            and is calculated according to the following steps:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
              If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> is <code>null</code>, return
              <code>null</code>.
            </li>
            <li>
              If <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> &lt; <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a></code>
              the result depends on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> as follows,
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>
                  If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> is <span class="prop-value">backwards</span> or <span class="prop-value">both</span>,
                </dt>
                <dd>
                  return zero.
                </dd><dd>
                </dd><dt>
                  Otherwise,
                </dt>
                <dd>
                  return <code>null</code>.
                </dd>
              </dl>
            </li>
            <li>
              If <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> &lt; <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active
              duration</a></code>, return <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a></code>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Otherwise, the result depends on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> as follows,
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>
                  If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill mode</a> is <span class="prop-value">forwards</span> or <span class="prop-value">both</span>,
                </dt>
                <dd>
                  return the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>.
                </dd><dd>
                </dd><dt>
                  Otherwise,
                </dt>
                <dd>
                  return <code>null</code>.
                </dd>
              </dl>
            </li>
          </ol>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="calculating-the-scaled-active-time">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.10.3.2 </span>Calculating the scaled active time</h5>
          <p>
            Before the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> can be converted to an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration
            time</a> we must factor in the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration
            start</a>.
            The result is called the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            In order to calculate the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> we first
            define the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start offset</a> as follows:
          </p>
          <blockquote>
            <dfn id="dfn-start-offset">start offset</dfn> =
              <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a></code>
          </blockquote>
          <p>
            The <dfn id="dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</dfn> is calculated according to
            the following steps:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
              If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> is <code>null</code>, return
              <code>null</code>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Return the scaled active time based on the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> as follows,
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
                    is negative,</dt>
                <dd>
                Return <code>(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> -
                              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>)
                        * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
                        + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start offset</a></code>.
                </dd>
                <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
                <dd>
                  Return <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a>
                  * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
                  + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start offset</a></code>.
                </dd>
            </dl></li>
          </ol>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="calculating-the-iteration-time">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.10.3.3 </span>Calculating the iteration time</h5>
          <p>
            The <dfn id="dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</dfn> is calculated according to the
            following steps:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
              If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> is <code>null</code>,
              return <code>null</code>.
            </li>
            <li>
              If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is zero, return zero.
            </li>
            <li>
              If <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start
              offset</a></code> is equal to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-repeated-duration">repeated duration</a>,
              and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> is not zero,
              and <code>(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a>)
              % 1</code> is zero,
              return the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Otherwise, return <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a>
              % <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a></code>.
            </li>
          </ol>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-current-iteration">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.10.4 </span>Calculating the current iteration</h4>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</dfn> can be calculated using the
          following steps:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> is <code>null</code>, return
            <code>null</code>.
          </li>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> is zero, return zero.
          </li>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is zero, return
            <code>floor(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a>)</code>.
          </li>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a> equals the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration
            duration</a>, return <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-start">iteration start</a>
            + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> - 1</code>.
          </li>
          <li>
            Return <code>floor(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> /
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>)</code>.
            <p class="note">
              If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is infinite, the
              result of <code>floor(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-scaled-active-time">scaled active time</a> /
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>)</code> will be zero as defined by
              IEEE 754-2008.
            </p>
          </li>
        </ol>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="direction-control">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.11 </span>Direction control</h3>
      <p>
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> may also be configured to run iterations in
        alternative directions using direction control.
        For this purpose, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> have a <dfn id="dfn-playback-direction">playback
        direction</dfn> parameter which takes one of the following values:
      </p>
      <ul>
        <li>normal,</li>
        <li>reverse,</li>
        <li>alternate, or</li>
        <li>alternate-reverse.</li>
      </ul>
      <p>
        The semantics of these values are incorporated into the calculation of
        the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed time</a> which follows.
      </p>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          A non-normative definition of these values is as follows:
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt>normal</dt>
          <dd>
            All iterations are played as specified.
          </dd>
          <dt>reverse</dt>
          <dd>
            All iterations are played in the reverse direction from the way
            they are specified.
          </dd>
          <dt>alternate</dt>
          <dd>
            Even iterations are played as specified, odd iterations are played
            in the reverse direction from the way they are specified.
          </dd>
          <dt>alternate-reverse</dt>
          <dd>
            Even iterations are played in the reverse direction from the way
            they are specified, odd iterations are played as specified.
          </dd>
        </dl>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-directed-time">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.11.1 </span>Calculating the directed time</h4>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-directed-time">directed time</dfn> is calculated from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration
          time</a> using the following steps:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a> is <code>null</code>, return
              <code>null</code>.
          </li><li>
            Calculate the <var>current direction</var> using the first
            matching condition from the following list:
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>
                If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-playback-direction">playback direction</a> is <code>normal</code>,
              </dt>
              <dd>Let the <var>current direction</var> be forwards.</dd>
              <dt>
                If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-playback-direction">playback direction</a> is <code>reverse</code>,
              </dt>
              <dd>Let the <var>current direction</var> be reverse.</dd>
              <dt>
                Otherwise,
              </dt>
              <dd>
                <ol>
                  <li>
                    Let <var>d</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>.
                  </li>
                  <li>
                    If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-playback-direction">playback direction</a> is
                    <code>alternate-reverse</code> increment
                    <var>d</var> by 1.
                  </li>
                  <li>
                    <p class="issue">
                      There used to be a step here which seemed to be adding
                      special handling for filling when the item ends on
                      a repeat boundary but it seems like that is taken care
                      of by the calcuation of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a> and
                      <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>.
                      Is anything actually needed here?
                    </p>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                    If <code><var>d</var> % 2 == 0</code>, let the
                    <var>current direction</var> be forwards, otherwise let
                    the <var>current direction</var> be reverse.
                  </li>
                </ol>
              </dd>
            </dl>
          </li>
          <li>
            If the <var>current direction</var> is forwards then return
            the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a>.
            <p>
              Otherwise, return the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>
              - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-time">iteration time</a>.
            </p>
          </li>
        </ol>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="time-transformations">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.12 </span>Time transformations</h3>
      <div id="scaling-the-time" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.1 </span>Scaling the time</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          It is often desirable to control the rate at which a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
          progresses.
          For example, easing the rate of animation can create a sense of
          momentum and produce a more natural effect.
          Conversely, in other situations such as when modelling a discrete
          change, a smooth transition is undesirable and instead it is necessary
          for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> to progress in a series of distinct steps.
        </p>
        <p>
          For such situations Web Animations provides <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a>
          that scale the progress of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">Timing functions</a> take an input time fraction and produce
          a scaled output time fraction.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/timing-function-example.svg" alt="Example of a timing function that produces an ease-in effect." width="350">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Example of a timing function that produces a ease-in effect.
          Given a input timing fraction of 0.7, the timing function scales the
          value to produce an output time fraction of 0.52.<br>
          By applying this timing function, time will appear to progress more
          slowly at first but then gradually progress more quickly.
        </p>
        <p>
          Such <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a> can be applied to an iteration of
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>.
        </p>
      </div></div>
      <div class="section" id="timing-functions">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.2 </span>Timing functions</h4>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-timing-function">timing function</dfn> takes an input time fraction in the range
          [0, 1] and produces an output time fraction whose range is unbounded
          (i.e. positive and negative infinity are permitted).
        </p>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> have one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a> associated with
          them.
          The default <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a> is the <dfn id="dfn-linear-timing-function">linear timing
          function</dfn> whose output is identical to its input.
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            We are considering introducing the concept of chained timing
            functions.
          </p>
          <p>
            A chained timing function is composed of a set of primitive timing
            functions, where each primitive timing function maps a limited
            portion of the input range to a portion of the output range.
            Available primitive timing functions include
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-cubic-b-zier-timing-function">cubic B&#xe9;zier timing functions</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-step-timing-function">step timing functions</a>
            and the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-linear-timing-function">linear timing function</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            A chained timing function can be configured to explicitly specify
            the input and output ranges of each primitive timing function, or to
            align the input ranges of the primitive timing functions with the
            offsets of the corresponding animation effect's keyframes or path
            segments.
          </p>
          <p>
            See <a href="http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/public-fx/2013AprJun/0184.html">section
            5 (Chained timing functions) of minuted discussion from Tokyo
              2013 F2F</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="scaling-using-a-cubic-b-zier-curve">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.3 </span>Scaling using a cubic B&#xe9;zier curve</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            A common method of producing easing effects is to use a cubic B&#xe9;zier
            curve to scale the time.
            The endpoints of the curve are fixed at (0, 0) and (1, 1) while two
            control points <var>P1</var> and <var>P2</var> define the shape of
            the curve.
            Provided the <var>x</var> values of <var>P1</var> and <var>P2</var>
            lie within the range [0, 1] such a curve produces a function that is
            used to map input times (the <var>x</var> values) onto output times
            (the <var>y</var> values).
            This arrangement is illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/cubic-bezier-timing-curve.svg" alt="A cubic Bezier curve used as a timing function." width="500">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            A cubic B&#xe9;zier curve used as a timing function.<br>
            The shape of the curve is determined by the location of the control
            points <var>P1</var> and <var>P2</var>.<br>
            Input time fractions serve as <var>x</var> values of the curve,
            whilst the <var>y</var> values are the output time fractions.
          </p>
          <p>
            Some example cubic B&#xe9;zier timing functions are illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/curve-keywords.svg" alt="The timing functions produced by keyword values." width="500">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            The timing functions produced by each of the keyword values
            associated with cubic B&#xe9;zier timing functions accepted by the
            <a href="#widl-Timing-timingFunction" class="idlType"><code>Timing.timingFunction</code></a>
            member from the <a href="#script-interface">script interface</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-cubic-b-zier-timing-function">cubic B&#xe9;zier timing function</dfn> is a type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing
          function</a> defined by four real numbers that specify the two control
          points, <var>P1</var> and <var>P2</var>, of a cubic B&#xe9;zier curve whose
          end points are fixed at (0, 0) and (1, 1).
          The x coordinates of <var>P1</var> and <var>P2</var> are
          restricted to the range [0, 1].
        </p>
        <p>
          The evaluation of this curve is covered in many sources such as
          [<cite><a href="#bib-FUND-COMP-GRAPHICS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">FUND-COMP-GRAPHICS</a></cite>].
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            It has been proposed to extend <code>cubic-bezier</code> to allow
            multiple segments, using syntax such as the following:
          </p>
          <pre>            <code>cubic-bezier( [ &lt;number&gt;{6} ; ]* &lt;number&gt;{4} )</code>
          </pre>
          <p>
            (i.e. the curve starts at (0, 0); each segment is defined by six
            numbers where the start point is the end of the previous segment and
            the numbers define the two control points and the end point. The
            last segment is defined by four numbers since the end point is fixed
            at (1, 1).)
          </p>
          <p>
            This would provide a simpler and more compact syntax for tools
            trying to map arbitrary curves (e.g. bounce functions) to timing
            functions than trying to construct the corresponding chained timing
            function.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="timing-in-discrete-steps">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.4 </span>Timing in discrete steps</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            It is possible to scale a timed item's timing so that the timed item
            occurs in a series of discrete steps using a stepping function.
          </p>
          <p>
            Some example step timing functions are illustrated below.
          </p>
          <div class="figure">
            <img src="img/step-timing-func-examples.svg" alt="Example step timing functions." width="700">
          </div>
          <p class="caption">
            Example step timing functions.
            In each case the domain is the input time fraction whilst the range
            represents the output time fraction produced by the step
            function.<br>
            The first row shows the function for each transition point when only
            one step is specified whilst the second row shows the same for three
            steps.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-step-timing-function">step timing function</dfn> is a type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a>
          that divides the input time into a specified number of intervals that
          are equal in duration.
          The output time, starting at zero, rises by an amount equal to the
          interval duration once during each interval at the transition point
          which may be either the start, midpoint, or end of the interval.
        </p>
        <p>
          In keeping with Web Animation's model for endpoint exclusive
          interval timing (see <a href="#interval-timing" class="sectionRef">section 3.8.4 Interval timing</a>), the output time at the transition point is
          the time <em>after</em> applying the increase (i.e. the top of the
          step).
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="paced-timing">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.5 </span>Paced timing</h4>
        <div class="todo">
          <p>Insert a nice diagram showing how this works</p>
        </div>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-paced-timing-function">paced timing function</dfn> scales the input time such that the
          resulting time values cause a <dfn id="dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</dfn> that is
          animated by a specified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>, referred to as the
          <dfn id="dfn-paced-effect">paced effect</dfn>,
          to change at a constant rate over the period of time for which the
          paced timing function applies.
        </p>
        <p>
          The syntax for specifying a paced timing function is:
          <code>paced(<a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/css3-syntax/#property">&lt;property&gt;</a>)</code>.
          The <code>&lt;property&gt;</code> argument is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced
          property</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-timing-function">paced timing function</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            For example, <code>paced(transform)</code> would indicate that the
            time should be scaled such that changes to the <span class="prop-name">transform</span> property occur at a constant
            rate.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-effect">paced effect</a> is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> specified on
          the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> where the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-timing-function">paced timing function</a> is
          applied.
          As a result, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-timing-function">paced timing functions</a> can only be used on
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a> and not other types of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          If <em>any</em> of the following conditions is true, the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-linear-timing-function">linear timing function</a> is used for the purpose of timing model
          calculations:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li>there is no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-effect">paced effect</a> (because the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is
              not an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> or does not specify an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
              effect</a>), or
          </li><li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</a> is not one of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target
              properties</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-effect">paced effect</a>, or
          </li><li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</a> is not <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-interpolable">interpolable</a>, or
          </li><li>the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</a> is not a valid property.
        </li></ul>
        <div class="section" id="evaluating-a-paced-timing-function">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.12.5.1 </span>Evaluating a paced timing function</h5>
          <p>
            The result of evaluating a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-paced-timing-function">paced timing function</a> at
            <var>input time</var> is calculated as follows:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
              Let <var>length list</var> be a sequence of length values
              calculated using the rules defined in <a href="#calculating-the-length-between-two-property-values" class="sectionRef">section 3.12.5.2 Calculating the length between two property values</a>
              for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</a> between each pair of keyframes
              that refers to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-referenced-property">referenced property</a> in a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe
              animation effect</a>,
              or between each path segment in a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation effect</a>.
              <p class="issue">
                Need to confirm this approach is actually backwards-compatible
                with SVG with regards to motion-path behavior.
              </p>
            </li><li>
              If the number of items in <var>length list</var> is 1 or less let
              the output of the timing function be <var>input time</var> and
              terminate these steps.
            </li><li>
              Let <var>total length</var> be the sum of values in
              <var>length list</var>.
            </li><li>
              If <var>total length</var> is zero let
              the output of the timing function be <var>input time</var> and
              terminate these steps.
            </li><li>
              Let <var>distance</var> be
              <code><var>input time</var> &#xd7; <var>total length</var></code>.
            </li><li>
              Let <var>current position</var> be 0.
            </li><li>
              Let <var>current distance</var> be 0.
            </li><li>
              Let <var>current length</var> be the first value in <var>length
              list</var>.
            </li><li>While <var>distance</var> &gt; <code><var>current distance</var>
              + <var>current length</var></code>, perform the following steps:
              <ol>
                <li>Increment <var>current position</var> by 1.
                </li><li>Increase <var>current distance</var> by <var>current
                    length</var>.
                </li><li>Let <var>current length</var> be the value at
                    position <var>current position</var> in <var>length
                    list</var>.
              </li></ol>
            </li><li>
              The output of the paced timing function is the result of
              evaluating:
              <code><var>current distance</var> / <var>total length</var> + 
                (<var>distance</var> - <var>current distance</var>) / 
                <var>current length</var></code>
          </li></ol>
          <p class="issue">
            Is this algorithm necessary? Would a prose description suffice?
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="calculating-the-length-between-two-property-values">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.12.5.2 </span>Calculating the length between two property values</h5>
          <p>
            The length between any two property values depends on the type of
            values as follows:
          </p>
          <dl>
            <dt>For numeric values,</dt>
            <dd>
              length is defined as the absolute value of the
              difference between two values.
              <p class="todo">
                Need to explain how this applies to length values.
              </p>
            </dd>
            <dt>For colors,</dt>
            <dd>
              length is defined as the result of evaluating the following
              expression
              <div role="math" aria-describedby="math-color-length">
              <div style="text-align: center;" aria-readonly="true" role="textbox" class="MathJax_SVG_Display"><span id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" class="MathJax_SVG" style="display: xlink:href="#MJMAIN-62"></use></g></g><use y="0" x="3809" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-29"></use><use y="688" x="5944" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-32" transform="scale(0.7071067811865476)"></use></g><use y="0" x="16218" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-2B"></use><g transform="translate(17223,0)"><use xlink:href="#MJMAIN-32"></use><use y="0" x="505" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-35"></use><use y="0" x="1010" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-35"></use></g><use y="0" x="18961" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-D7"></use><g transform="translate(19966,0)"><use xlink:href="#MJMAIN-32"></use><use y="0" x="505" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-35"></use><use y="0" x="1010" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-35"></use></g><use y="0" x="21703" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-D7"></use><g transform="translate(22708,0)"><use xlink:href="#MJMAIN-28"></use><g transform="translate(394,0)"><use xlink:href="#MJMAIN-61"></use><use y="0" x="505" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-61"></use><use y="0" x="1232" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-2212"></use><g transform="translate(2237,0)"><use xlink:href="#MJMAIN-61"></use><use y="0" x="505" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-62"></use></g></g><use y="0" x="3697" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-29"></use><use y="688" x="5786" xlink:href="#MJMAIN-32" transform="scale(0.7071067811865476)"></use></g></g></g></svg></span></div><script id="MathJax-Element-1" type="math/mml"><math display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
              <mrow>
                <msqrt>
                  <msup>
                    <mrow>
                      <mfenced separators="," close=")" open="(">
                        <mrow><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">ra</mi><mo>-</mo><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">rb</mi></mrow></mfenced>
                    </mrow><mn>2</mn>
                  </msup>
                  <mo>+</mo>
                  <msup>
                    <mrow>
                      <mfenced separators="," close=")" open="(">
                        <mrow><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">ga</mi><mo>-</mo><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">gb</mi></mrow></mfenced>
                    </mrow><mn>2</mn>
                  </msup>
                  <mo>+</mo>
                  <msup>
                    <mrow>
                      <mfenced separators="," close=")" open="(">
                        <mrow><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">ba</mi><mo>-</mo><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">bb</mi></mrow></mfenced>
                    </mrow><mn>2</mn>
                  </msup>
                  <mo>+</mo>
                  <mn>255</mn><mo>&#xd7;</mo><mn>255</mn><mo>&#xd7;</mo>
                  <msup>
                    <mrow>
                      <mfenced separators="," close=")" open="(">
                        <mrow><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">aa</mi><mo>-</mo><mi _moz-math-font-style="normal">ab</mi></mrow>
                      </mfenced>
                    </mrow><mn>2</mn>
                  </msup>
                </msqrt>
              </mrow>
              </math></script>
              <pre id="math-color-length">sqrt((ra - rb)^2 + (ga - gb)^2 + (ba - bb)^2 + 255*255*(aa - ab)^2)</pre>
              </div>
              <p>
                where the colors between which the length is to be measured are
                <code>rgba(ra, ga, ba, aa)</code> and
                <code>rgba(rb, gb, bb, ab)</code> respectively.
              </p>
            </dd>
            <dt>For transform values,</dt>
            <dd>
              <p>
                The definition of length for transform values depends on whether
                adjacent keyframe values of the transform property have matching
                first components.
                If the components are translate functions, then euclidean
                distance between the two translation vectors is used. 
                If the components are scale functions, then the absolute
                difference between the average scale values is used.
                If the components are rotate functions, then the absolute
                difference between rotation angles is used.
              </p>
              <p>
                If the components match but are not scale, rotate or translate
                functions, then the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-linear-timing-function">linear timing function</a> is used
                for the purpose of timing model calculations.
              </p>
              <p>
                If the components do not match, then interpolation between the 
                components will require matrix decomposition.
                In this case the length is calculated using the euclidean
                distance between the translate components of the decomposed
                matrices.
              </p>
              <p class="todo">
                Need a reference for euclidean distance.
              </p>
              <p class="todo">
                This only refers to keyframe values.
                Need to explain what to do for paths.
              </p>
            </dd>
          </dl>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-transformed-time">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.12.6 </span>Calculating the transformed time</h4>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</dfn> is calculated from the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed time</a> using the following steps:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed time</a> is <code>null</code>,
            return <code>null</code>.
          </li>
          <li>Let <var>iteration fraction</var> be the result of
              evaluating <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directed-time">directed time</a> / <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration
              duration</a></code> unless <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is
              zero, in which case let <var>iteration fraction</var> be
              zero.</li>
          <li>Let <var>scaled fraction</var> be the result of
              evaluating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a>
              with <var>iteration fraction</var> as the input time
              fraction.
          </li><li>Return the result of evaluating <code><var>scaled
              fraction</var> * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a></code>.
        </li></ol>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="grouping-and-synchronization">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.13 </span>Grouping and synchronization</h3>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          While it is possible to set the timing properties of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          items</a> individually, it is often useful to synchronize <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          items</a> so that they share common timing properties and maintain
          their temporal relationship.  This is achieved using a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing
          group</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          A simple example is illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-delay.svg" alt="Using groups to share common timing properties." width="800">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Using groups to share common timing properties.<br>
          (a) Shows setting a delay of 5 seconds on individual animations.<br>
          (b) Produces the same effect by setting the delay on the group.
        </p>
        <p>
          When a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> is directly associated with
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> associated with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing
          group</a> can be seeked, paused, and stopped as a unit.
        </p>
      </div>
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-timing-group">timing group</dfn> is a type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> that contains
        an ordered sequence of zero or more <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> known as <dfn id="dfn-child-timed-item" title="child timed item">child timed items</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        At a given moment, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> may be a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a>
        of at most one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> known as the <dfn id="dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing
        group</dfn>.
        The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> cannot be the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
        item</a> as the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a> itself.
      </p>
      <p>
        By nesting <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a> it is possible to create hierarchical
        tree structures.
        The following terms are used to describe the parts and properties of
        such structures and are defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-DOM4" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">DOM4</a></cite>]:
      </p>
      <ul>
        <li><dfn id="dfn-tree-order"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-order">tree order</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-root"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-root">root</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-ancestor"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-ancestor">ancestor</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-descendant"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-descendant">descendant</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-inclusive-ancestor"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-inclusive-ancestor">inclusive ancestor</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-inclusive-descendant"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-inclusive-descendant">inclusive descendant</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-next-sibling"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-next-sibling">next
        sibling</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-previous-sibling"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-previous-sibling">previous
        sibling</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-first-child"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-first-child">first child</a></dfn>
        </li><li><dfn id="dfn-last-child"><a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/dom/#concept-tree-last-child">last child</a></dfn>
      </li></ul>
      <p class="note">
        Note that in applying these definitions to <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a>, the term
        <em>parent</em> refers exclusively to a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> and
        does not include the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> which with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> may be
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-directly-associated-with-a-player" title="directly associated with a player">directly associated</a>
        despite the fact that conceptually the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> acts as a parent
        time source.
      </p>
      <p>
        The temporal relationship between a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a> and its
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> is incorporated in the definition of
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited time</a> (see <a href="#local-time-and-inherited-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.6.2 Local time and inherited time</a>).
      </p>
      <div id="relationship-of-group-time-to-child-time" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.13.1 </span>Relationship of group time to child time</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          The timing of the children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> is based on the
          timing of the group.
          Specifically, times for the children are based on the parent's
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>.
          With regards to repetition, this means the children operate
          <em>inside</em> an iteration of the parent.
        </p>
        <p>
          For example, if a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> has an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> of
          2, then the children of of the group will all play twice since they
          effectively play <em>inside</em> the group's iterations.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-repetition.svg" alt="The effect of multiple iterations on the children of a
                    group." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Since children of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> base their timing on the
          group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>, when the group repeats, the
          children play again.
        </p>
        <p>
          Note that even in this case, the child <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> still have
          only <em>one</em> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          However, as a result of the parent's timing, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active
          interval</a> is played twice.
        </p>
        <p>
          If an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> is specified for the children of a group
          as well as for the group itself, the effect is as if the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration
          count</a> of the group was multiplied with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a>
          of the children.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-repetition-and-animation-repetition.svg" alt="Iteration counts are multiplicative." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Specifying an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> of 2 on an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>
          and an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a> of 3 on one of its children results in
          that child playing 6 times.
        </p>
        <p>
          A further result of the children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> basing their
          timing on the group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> is that they cannot
          animate outside of the group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          This is because the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> of a group will not
          change outside its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
          This allows groups to <em>clip</em> the playback of their children.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-clipping.svg" alt="Groups clip the active interval of contained children." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          In the first instance, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> has a negative delay and an
          infinite <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-count">iteration count</a>.<br>
          However, when a similar <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is placed inside a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing
          group</a> with a specified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> it has the effect
          of clipping the child <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Some further consequences of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> children basing their
          timing on their parent group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> are:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li>
            Setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a> of
            a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> will speed up or slow down all children.
          </li>
          <li>
            Changing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-playback-direction">playback direction</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> will
            change the direction of all children.
          </li>
          <li>
            Applying a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a> to a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> will
            affect the progress of all children.
          </li>
        </ul>
      </div></div>
      <div id="types-of-timing-groups" class="informative section">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.13.2 </span>Types of timing groups</h4><div class="informative-bg"><p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">Timing groups</a> can be used to provide different kinds of
          synchronization behavior for their children.
          For example, one type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> runs its children in
          parallel, whilst another type runs the children in sequence.
        </p>
        <p>
          Compare the two arrangements illustrated below:
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-types.svg" alt="Two types of timing groups." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Two types of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a>.<br>
          (a) is a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</a> where all the children run
              simultaneously.<br>
          (b) is a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> where the children run in turn.
        </p>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">Timing groups</a> can also contain other <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a> which
          allows for more sophisticated synchronization.
          An example is illustrated below.
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/grouping-nesting.svg" alt="Nesting of timing groups." width="600">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> that contains a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing
          group</a> as a child.<br>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</a> waits for the previous child of the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> to finish, and then the children of the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</a> play simultaneously.
          After they have finished the next child of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing
          group</a> plays.
        </p>
        <p>
          Web Animations defines two types of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a>.
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">Parallel timing groups</a></dt>
          <dd>
            Children of the group play simultaneously.
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of each child
            coincides with the beginning of the group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-interval">iteration
            interval</a>.
          </dd>
          <dt><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">Sequence timing groups</a></dt>
          <dd>
            Children of the group play in turn beginning with the first child
            and proceeding to the last.
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of each child is
            set to the end of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> of the previous
            sibling.
          </dd>
        </dl>
      </div></div>
      <div class="section" id="parallel-timing-groups">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.13.3 </span>Parallel timing groups</h4>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</dfn> is a type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>
          that schedules its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed items</a> such that they play
          simultaneously.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="the-start-time-of-children-of-a-parallel-timing-group">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.13.3.1 </span>The start time of children of a parallel timing group</h5>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child
            timed item</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</a> is zero.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the-intrinsic-iteration-duration-of-a-parallel-timing-group">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.13.3.2 </span>The intrinsic iteration duration of a parallel timing group</h5>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing
            group</a> is based on the time when the last <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a>
            completes its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> and is calculated using the
            following procedure.
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>
