              <p>Define the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> as
              :</p>
              <blockquote>
                <dfn id="dfn-end-time">end time</dfn> =
                <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
                delay</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a></code>
              </blockquote>
            </li>
            <li>
              <p>
                The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> depends on the number of
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed items</a> as follows,
              </p>
              <dl class="switch">
                <dt>If the group has no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed items</a>,</dt>
                <dd>
                  the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> is zero.
                </dd>
                <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
                <dd>
                  <ol>
                    <li>Let <var>maximum end time</var> be the maximum value
                        after calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end time</a> of each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child
                        timed item</a> in the group.</li>
                    <li>The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> is the result of
                        evaluating <code>max(0, <var>maximum end
                        time</var>)</code>.</li>
                  </ol>
                </dd>
              </dl>
            </li>
          </ol>
          <p class="note">
            Note that for children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parallel-timing-group">parallel timing group</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> will always be zero but
            it is included in the definition of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end time</a> here since the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end time</a> is also used to define the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration
            duration</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a>
            (see <a href="#the-intrinsic-iteration-duration-of-a-sequence-timing-group" class="sectionRef">section 3.13.4.2 The intrinsic iteration duration of a sequence timing group</a>).
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="sequence-timing-groups">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.13.4 </span>Sequence timing groups</h4>
        <p>
          A <dfn id="dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</dfn> is a type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>
          that schedules its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed items</a> such that they play in
          turn following their order in the group.
          This ordering is achieved by adjusting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed
          item</a> in the group.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="the-start-time-of-children-of-a-sequence-timing-group">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.13.4.1 </span>The start time of children of a sequence timing group</h5>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child
            timed item</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end
            time</a> of the child's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-sibling">previous sibling</a>.
            If the child has no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-sibling">previous sibling</a> the start time is zero.
          </p>
          <div class="note">
            <p>
              When the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> is positive infinity the behavior
              for calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-end-time">end time</a> of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> and
              the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of subsequent
              children follows the usual behavior defined by IEEE 754-2008.
              As a result, if any of the children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing
              group</a> has an infinite <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>, any children
              that occur later in the sequence will not play.
            </p>
            <p>
              Similarly, the above definition does not restrict
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start times</a> to positive
              values and hence some children may not play due to a negative
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> on children that occur earlier in the group
              since their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> may end before the group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a>.
            </p>
            <p class="todo">
              Need to define if events fire in this case.
            </p>
          </div>
          <div class="informative informative-bg">
            <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
              Because the start of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> is based on the
              sum of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> <em>and</em> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active intervals</a> of
              children of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> need not run in strict
              sequence but can be shifted back and forth by using the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a> as shown in the following diagram.
            </p>
            <div class="figure">
              <img src="img/sequence-groups-and-start-delays.svg" alt="Using negative start delays to overlap children of seq
                    groups" width="600">
            </div>
            <p>
              A negative <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> can be used to cause the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active
              interval</a> of two children to overlap.  Note that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a> affects the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start
              time</a> of subsequent children in the group.
            </p>
          </div>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the-intrinsic-iteration-duration-of-a-sequence-timing-group">
          <h5><span class="secno">3.13.4.2 </span>The intrinsic iteration duration of a sequence timing group</h5>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing
            group</a> is equivalent to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-start-time" title="timed item start time">start time</a> of a hypothetical
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a> appended to the group's children calculated
            according to the definition in <a href="#the-start-time-of-children-of-a-sequence-timing-group" class="sectionRef">section 3.13.4.1 The start time of children of a sequence timing group</a> unless that produces a negative value, in
            which case the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> is zero.
          </p>
          <p>
            As a result, if the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a> has no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child
            timed items</a> the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intrinsic-iteration-duration">intrinsic iteration duration</a> will be
            zero.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="animations">
      <h3><span class="secno">3.14 </span>Animations</h3>
      <p>
        <dfn id="dfn-animation" title="animation">Animations</dfn> are a kind of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
        that apply an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> to an element or pseudo-element
        such as <code>::before</code> and <code>::first-line</code> [<cite><a href="#bib-SELECT" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SELECT</a></cite>]
        referred to as the <dfn id="dfn-target-element">target element</dfn>.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-time-fraction">
        <h4><span class="secno">3.14.1 </span>Calculating the time fraction</h4>
        <p>
          Before passing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> to
          its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> it is converted to a <em>time
          fraction</em>.
          The <dfn id="dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</dfn> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is calculated
          according to the following steps:
        </p>
        <dl class="switch">
          <dt>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is zero,
          </dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> is as follows,
            </p>
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>
                If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> &lt; <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a>,
              </dt>
              <dd>
                Return the result of recalculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>
                using a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> less than <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> (e.g.
                <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start delay</a> - 1</code>) and an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration
                duration</a> of 1.
              </dd>
              <dt>
                Otherwise,
              </dt>
              <dd>
                <ol>
                  <li>Let <var>normalized active duration</var> be the result of
                      recalculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a> using an
                      <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> of 1.
                  </li><li>Return the result of recalculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed
                      time</a> using a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local time</a> of <var>normalized
                      active duration</var> and an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> of
                      1.
                </li></ol>
              </dd>
            </dl>
          </dd>
          <dt>
            Otherwise,
          </dt>
          <dd>
            Return <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> / <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> unless
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a> is <code>null</code>, in which case return
            <code>null</code>.
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p class="note">
          Since <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a> are allowed to produce output times
          outside the range [0, 1] it is possible that the value calculated for
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> also lies outside this range.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>
    </div> <!-- End of timing model -->

    <div class="section" id="animation-model">
      <!--OddPage--><h2><span class="secno">4. </span>Animation model</h2>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          The Web Animations <em>animation model</em> takes the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time
          fractions</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> values produced by the
          <em>timing model</em> for a given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> and applies it as
          the input to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The output of each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> is then combined with other
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a> using an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> before being
          applied to the target properties (see <a href="#combining-animations" class="sectionRef">section 4.2 Combining animations</a>).
        </p>
      </div>

    <div class="section" id="animation-effects">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.1 </span>Animation effects</h3>
      <p>
        An <dfn id="dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</dfn> takes a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> and
        a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> value and uses them to calculate an
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> for its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a>.
        Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> may have at most one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>
        associated with it.
      </p>
      <p>
        Since the result of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> is based on the
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> value, it is updated
        whenever the timing model is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sampling" title="sampling">sampled</a>.
        Note that changes to the timing model caused by using the <a href="#script-interface">programming interface</a> do <em>not</em> cause
        the animation model (and hence <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a>) to be updated
        as described in <a href="#script-execution-and-live-updates-to-the-model" class="sectionRef">section 6.24 Script execution and live updates to the model</a>.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="target-properties">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.1.1 </span>Target properties</h4>
        <p>
          Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> can have zero or more associated
          <dfn id="dfn-target-properties">target properties</dfn>.
          Not all properties may be animated by an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>.
          Properties that may be animated by an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> are 
          defined as <dfn id="dfn-animatable">animatable</dfn>.
          The set of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animatable">animatable</a> properties is is defined in <a href="#animatable-properties" class="sectionRef">section 4.5 Animatable properties</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          An <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> that targets a property that is not
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animatable">animatable</a> will have no effect on the property.
          However, an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> that applies such an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effect</a> will still exhibit the usual behavior for a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          item</a> such as firing <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing events</a> and occupying time in
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sequence-timing-group">sequence timing group</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="target-property-types">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.1.2 </span>Target property types</h4>
        <p>
          The specific operations involved in animating a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties" title="target properties">target property</a> differ based on the
          <dfn id="dfn-property-type">property type</dfn>.
          For example, the specific procedure for animating a property that
          specifies a color will differ from a property that specifies a length.
          Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animatable">animatable</a> property defines one or more <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property
          types</a> to use when animating.
        </p>
        <p>
          In order to produce a smooth change between property values,
          a procedure for <dfn id="dfn-interpolation">interpolation</dfn> is required.
          A given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> is <dfn id="dfn-interpolable">interpolable</dfn> if there is
          a procedure defined to interpolate between two values of that type.
        </p>
        <p>
          In order to support <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation">accumulation</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">additive composition</a>,
          a procedure for <dfn id="dfn-addition">addition</dfn> is required.
          A given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> is <dfn id="dfn-additive">additive</dfn> if there is
          a procedure defined to add two values of that type.
        </p>
        <p>
          An initial list of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property types</a> and their procedures for
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-interpolation">interpolation</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-addition">addition</a> is given in <a href="#animation-of-property-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6 Animation of property types</a>.
          In addition to this initial list, specifications that define CSS
          properties may provide additional property types to define the
          procedures for interpolation and addition of the values of those
          properties.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="intermediate-animation-values">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.1.3 </span>Intermediate animation values</h4>
        <p>
          Given a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a>, a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>, and an
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>, an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> produces
          an <dfn id="dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</dfn> for each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animatable">animatable</a>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties" title="target properties">target property</a>.
          Before being applied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a>,
          these <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> are composed together using
          the process defined in <a href="#combining-animations" class="sectionRef">section 4.2 Combining animations</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            The use of the term 'value' here is misleading, as the output of
            the effect stage can not be resolved to a concrete value until it
            is composited with an underlying value. This takes place in the
            compositing stage, when the animation stack is resolved. It is
            therfore more accurate to describe the output of the effect stage
            as a set of values and corresponding composition operations, which
            are used to modify an underlying value. The same is true of the
            unaccumulated animation value.
          </p>
          <p>
            Use of this more precise terminology will also allow the algorithm
            for accumulation to be specified more precisely.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          An <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> is established by first
          calculating an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> and then applying
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation">accumulation</a> behavior.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="unaccumulated-animation-values">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.1.3.1 </span>Unaccumulated animation values</h5>
          <p>
            The <dfn id="dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</dfn> is the result of
            evaluating an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> for a given <a>target
            property</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>
            <em>independent</em> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>.
            The procedure for calculating this value depends on the specific
            type of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> and is defined subsequently (see <a href="#the-unaccumulated-animation-value-of-a-keyframe-animation-effect" class="sectionRef">section 4.3.1 The unaccumulated animation value of a keyframe animation effect</a> and <a href="#the-unaccumulated-animation-value-of-a-path-animation-effect" class="sectionRef">section 4.4.1 The unaccumulated animation value of a path animation effect</a>).
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="accumulating-animation-values">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.1.3.2 </span>Accumulating animation values</h5>
          <p>
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">Animation effects</a> may be defined such that as the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> that is applying them is <a href="#repeating">repeated</a>, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation
            value</a> builds on the value produced by previous iterations.
            This behavior is called <dfn id="dfn-accumulation">accumulation</dfn>.
          </p>
          <p>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation">accumulation</a> behavior of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> is
            specified by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>'s <dfn id="dfn-accumulation-operation">accumulation
            operation</dfn> property.
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation">accumulation operation</a> property takes one of the
            following two values.
          </p>
          <dl>
            <dt><dfn id="dfn-accumulation-operation-sum" title="accumulation operation sum">sum</dfn></dt>
            <dd>
              <p>
                The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> produced by the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> for a given property is the sum of the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> for the given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time
                fraction</a> and the final <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a>
                of the previous iteration (i.e. the result of evaluating the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a>
                of 1, and a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> of <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current
                iteration</a> - 1</code>).
              </p>
              <p>
                If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> is zero, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate
                animation value</a> is just the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation
                value</a>.
              </p>
            </dd>
            <dt><dfn id="dfn-accumulation-operation-none" title="accumulation operation none">none</dfn></dt>
            <dd>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
              effect</a> is just the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a>.
            </dd>
          </dl>
          <p>
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation">Accumulation</a> behavior is only applied for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target
            properties</a> that are <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-additive">additive</a>.
            For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a> whose values are not <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-additive">additive</a>,
            an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation">accumulation operation</a> of
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation-none" title="accumulation operation none">none</a> is used.
          </p>
          <p>
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation">Accumulation</a> behavior is only applied for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect" title="keyframe animation effect">keyframe animation effects</a>
            when the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> is uniform across all
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a>.
            For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect" title="keyframe animation effect">keyframe
            animation effects</a> where the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a>
            varies, an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation">accumulation operation</a> of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-accumulation-operation-none" title="accumulation operation none">none</a> is used.
          </p>
          <div class="issue">
            The definition of accumulation here needs review.
            The intention is to provide compatible behavior with SVG but also
            needs to account for the possibility of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a>
            whose final output value is not 1 (if we allow that), and possible
            differences in the way <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation" title="composition operation">composition</a> is defined.
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="combining-animations">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.2 </span>Combining animations</h3>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          After calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> for an
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> they are applied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effect</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Since it is possible for multiple <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation" title="animation">animations</a> to target the same property it is
          often necessary to combine the results of several <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a> together.
          This process is called <em>compositing</em> and is based on
          establishing an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> for each property targetted by
          an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-in-effect">in effect</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          After compositing the results of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a> together, the composited result is combined with other
          styles applied to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties" title="target properties">target
          property</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          An overview of this arrangement is illustrated below:
        </p>
        <div class="figure">
          <img src="img/animation-cascade.svg" alt="Overview of the application of intermediate animation values
                to their target properties" width="450">
        </div>
        <p class="caption">
          Overview of the application of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> to
          their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a>.<br>
          The results of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a> targetting the same property
          are composited together using an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a>.<br>
          The result of this composition is written to an override stylesheet
          that is more important than other stylesheets but less than any
          <code>!important</code> rules.
        </p>
        <p>
          For the first part of this operation&#x2014;combining <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate
          animation values</a> that target the same <a title="target property">property</a>&#x2014; it is necessary to
          determine both
          <em>how</em> the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a>
          associated with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a> are combined
          with one another,
          as well as the <em>order</em> in which they are applied, that is,
          their relative <em>priority</em>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The matter of <em>how</em> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> are
          combined is governed by any <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operations</a> associated
          with the corresponding <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The relative <em>priority</em> of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a>
          is determined by an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> established for each
          animated property.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="the-animation-stack">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.2.1 </span>The animation stack</h4>
        <p>
          Associated with each property <a title="target property">targetted</a>
          by one or more <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a> is an <dfn id="dfn-animation-stack">animation
          stack</dfn> that establishes the relative priority of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The relative priority of any two <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a>, <var>A</var> and <var>B</var>, within an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation
          stack</a> is established by comparing the properties of the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a> applying <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> as follows:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Let the <var>associated player</var> of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>
              be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> <a title="associated with a player">associated</a> with the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animation</a> that is applying the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> to
              the property with which this <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> is
              associated.
          </li><li>Sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> by applying the following
              conditions in turn until the order is resolved,
            <ol>
              <li>Sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> using any <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-animation-priority">custom
                  animation priority</a> specified for <var>A</var> and
                  <var>B</var> so that lower priorities sort first.
              </li><li>Sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time">player start
                  time</a> of the <var>associated player</var> of each
                  of <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> so that earlier times sort
                  first.
              </li><li>Sort by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-sequence-number">player sequence number</a> so that lower
                  sequence numbers sort first.
              </li><li>Sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> in <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-tree-order">tree order</a>.
           </li></ol>
        </li></ol>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">Animation effects</a> that sort earlier have <em>lower</em>
          priority.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="the-custom-animation-priority">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.2.1.1 </span>The custom animation priority</h5>
          <p>
            Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> has an associated numeric
            <dfn id="dfn-custom-animation-priority">custom animation priority</dfn> that is used to provide
            high-level control of animation priority for specifications layered
            on top of Web Animations.
            The initial value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-animation-priority">custom animation priority</a> is zero.
          </p>
          <div class="note">
            <p>
              Note that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-animation-priority">custom animation priority</a> is primarily
              intended to be used to prioritize animation effects at
              a high-level, such as to prioritize animations <em>by type</em>.
              For example, it can be used to ensure that CSS Animations always
              override CSS Transitions.
            </p>
            <p>
              It is possible to control animation priority at a lower-level by
              setting the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time">player start time</a> appropriately,
              (possibly after making compensatory adjustments to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a>) or influencing the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-sequence-number">player sequence number</a> by controlling when <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">players</a>
              are created.
            </p>
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-result-of-an-animation-stack">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.2.2 </span>Calculating the result of an animation stack</h4>
        <p>
          In order to calculate the final value of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a>,
          the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> of each
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> in the stack are combined in order of priority
          from lowest to highest priority.
        </p>
        <p>
          Each step in the process of evaluating an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> takes
          an <dfn id="dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</dfn> as input.
          The initial <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-base-value">base value</a> of the
          target property as defined in <a href="#combining-with-other-styles--the-override-stylesheet" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.4 Combining with other styles: the override stylesheet</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          For each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> in the stack, the appropriate
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>
          is combined with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> to produce a new value.
          This resulting value becomes the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> for combining
          the next <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> in the stack.
        </p>
        <p>
          The final value of an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a>, called the
          <dfn id="dfn-composited-value">composited value</dfn>, is simply the result of combining the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> of the final (highest priority)
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> in the stack with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>
          at that point.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-composition">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.2.3 </span>Animation composition</h4>
        <p>
          The specific operation used to combine an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation
          value</a> with an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> is determined by the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> that produced the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation
          value</a> and is called the <dfn id="dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</dfn>.
        </p>
        <p>
          This specification defines two common <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operations</a> as
          follows:
        </p>
        <dl>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-composition-operation-replace" title="composition operation replace">replace</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            The result of compositing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a>
            with the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> is simply the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate
            animation value</a>.
          </dd>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">add</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-addition" title="addition">added</a> to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>.
              For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property types</a> where
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-addition">addition</a> is defined such that it is not commutative, the
              order of the operands is <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>
              + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a></code>.
            </p>
            <p>
              If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation value</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>
              are not of the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a>, or if they are of the
              same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> but that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> is not
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-additive">additive</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-replace" title="composition operation replace">replace</a> behavior is
              applied.
            </p>
          </dd>
        </dl>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="combining-with-other-styles--the-override-stylesheet">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.2.4 </span>Combining with other styles: the override stylesheet</h4>
        <p>
          Applying a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composited-value">composited value</a> to a property depends on
          establishing an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-override-stylesheet">override stylesheet</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-override-stylesheet">override stylesheet</dfn> contains
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composited-value" title="composited value">composited animation values</a>
          and acts with a higher priority than all other stylesheets.
          However, <code>!important</code> rules from all other stylesheets act
          with a higher priority than the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-override-stylesheet">override stylesheet</a>.
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-override-stylesheet">override stylesheet</a> is regenerated each time the
          <a>animation model</a> is updated (see <a href="#animation-effects" class="sectionRef">section 4.1 Animation effects</a>).
        </p>
        <p>
        </p>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composited-value">composited value</a> calculated for a property is applied
          using the following process.
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Calculate the <dfn id="dfn-base-value">base value</dfn> of the property as
              the value generated for that property by computing the <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/CSS2/cascade.html#used-value">used
              value</a> [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS21" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS21</a></cite>] for that property in the absence of the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-override-stylesheet">override stylesheet</a>.</li>
          <li>Establish the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a> for the property (see <a href="#the-animation-stack" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.1 The animation stack</a>).</li>
          <li>Calculate the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composited-value">composited value</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation
              stack</a> passing in the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-base-value">base value</a> of the property as the
              initial <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> (see <a href="#calculating-the-result-of-an-animation-stack" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.2 Calculating the result of an animation stack</a>).</li>
          <li>Insert the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composited-value">composited value</a> into the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-override-stylesheet">override
              stylesheet</a>.</li>
        </ol>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="keyframe-animation-effects">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.3 </span>Keyframe animation effects</h3>
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe animation effect</dfn> is an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>
        that produces <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-intermediate-animation-value">intermediate animation values</a> for its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target
        properties</a> by interpolating between a series of property values
        positioned at fractional offsets.
      </p>
      <p>
        Each set of property values indexed by a positional offset is called
        a <dfn id="dfn-keyframe">keyframe</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The <dfn id="dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe">positional offset of a keyframe</dfn> is a value in the range
        [0, 1].
        The list of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> for a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe animation effect</a> is
        sorted in ascending order by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset of each
        keyframe</a>.
      </p>
      <p class="note">
        Unlike CSS syntax, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a> are <em>not</em> directly
        associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a>.
        Rather, this is achieved by setting a chain of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a>
        on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> (proposal for this is still in the works).
      </p>
      <p>
        If, due to a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing function</a> specified on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
        item</a> from which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> is derived, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time
        fraction</a> lies outside the range [0, 1], the specified
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> property values are extrapolated to cover the extended
        range.
      </p>
      <p>
        The behavior when <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> overlap or have unsupported values
        is defined in <a href="#the-unaccumulated-animation-value-of-a-keyframe-animation-effect" class="sectionRef">section 4.3.1 The unaccumulated animation value of a keyframe animation effect</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe animation effect</a> has an associated <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition
        operation</a> that specifies how it is combined with other <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
        effects</a> in the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-stack">animation stack</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        Furthermore, each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> may also have an associated
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> that is applied to all values specified in
        that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a>.
        If no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> is specified for a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a>,
        the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> specified for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe
        animation effect</a> is used.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="the-unaccumulated-animation-value-of-a-keyframe-animation-effect">              
        <h4><span class="secno">4.3.1 </span>The unaccumulated animation value of a keyframe animation effect</h4>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> of a single property
          referenced by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe animation effect</a> as one of its
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-properties">target properties</a>, for a given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> and
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> is calculated as follows.
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Let <var>target property</var> be the property for which the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> is to be calculated.
          </li><li>If <var>target property</var> is not <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animatable">animatable</a> abort the
              procedure since the effect cannot be applied.</li>
          <li>Let <var>time fraction</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> for which
              the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> is to be calculated.</li>
          <li>Let <var>underlying value</var> be the current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying
              value</a>.
          </li><li>Define the <dfn id="dfn-neutral-value-for-composition">neutral value for composition</dfn> as a value
              which, when combined with an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> using the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">add</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition
              operation</a>, produces the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a>.
              <p class="note">
                Note that this definition does not require determining
                a suitable zero value for each possible <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a>.
                This behavior could be realized, for example, by use of
                a sentinel value.
              </p>
          </li><li>Let <var>property-specific keyframes</var> be a copy of the list
              of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> specified on the effect.</li>
          <li>Remove any <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> from <var>property-specific
              keyframes</var> that do not have a property value for
              <var>target property</var>.
          </li><li>If <var>property-specific keyframes</var> is empty, return
              <var>underlying value</var>.
          </li><li>If there is no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset</a> of
              0, create a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a positional offset of 0,
              a property value set to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-neutral-value-for-composition">neutral value for composition</a>,
              and a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition
              operation add">add</a>, and add it to the beginning of
              <var>property-specific keyframes</var>.
          </li><li>Similarly, if there is no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset</a> of
              1, create a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a positional offset of 1,
              a property value set to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-neutral-value-for-composition">neutral value for composition</a>,
              and a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition
              operation add">add</a>, and append it to the end of
              <var>property-specific keyframes</var>.
          </li><li>Iterate over each <var>keyframe</var> in <var>property-specific
              keyframes</var> and for each <var>keyframe</var>, if:
              <ul>
                <li><var>keyframe</var> has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a>
                    of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">add</a>, or
                </li><li><var>keyframe</var> has no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a>
                    and the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition operation</a> of this <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe-animation-effect">keyframe
                    animation effect</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">add</a>
              </li></ul>
              perform the following steps:
              <ol>
                <li>Let <var>value to add</var> be the property value of
                    <var>target property</var> specified on <var>keyframe</var>.
                </li><li>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> of <var>underlying value</var>
                    and <var>value to add</var> is the same and is
                    <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-additive">additive</a>, set the property value of <var>target
                    property</var> for <var>keyframe</var> to
                    <code><var>underlying value</var> + <var>value to
                    add</var></code>.
              </li></ol>
          </li><li>If <var>time fraction</var> &lt; 0 and there is more
              than one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>property-specific
              keyframes</var> with a positional offset of 0, return the property
              value for <var>target property</var> of the first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a>
              in <var>property-specific keyframes</var>.</li>
          <li>If <var>time fraction</var> &#x2265; 1 and there is more than one
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>property-specific keyframes</var> with
              a positional offset of 1, return the property value for
              <var>target property</var> of the last <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in
              <var>property-specific keyframes</var>.</li>
          <li>Let <var>start keyframe</var> be the last <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in
              <var>property-specific keyframes</var> whose positional offset is
              less than or equal to <var>time fraction</var> and less than 1.
              If there is no such <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> (because, for example, the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> is negative), let <var>start keyframe</var>
              be the last <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> whose positional offset is 0.</li>
          <li>Let <var>end keyframe</var> be the next <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in
              <var>property-specific keyframes</var> after <var>start
              keyframe</var>.</li>
          <li>If the pair of property values specified by <var>start
              keyframe</var> and <var>end keyframe</var>
              differ in <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> or have the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property
              type</a> but that type is not <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-interpolable">interpolable</a>,
              then return the property value of <var>start keyframe</var>
              unless <var>time fraction</var> is greater than or equal to 1, in
              which case return the property value of <var>end
              keyframe</var>.</li>
          <li>Let <var>start offset</var> be the positional offset of <var>start
              keyframe</var>.</li>
          <li>Let <var>end offset</var> be the offset of <var>end
              keyframe</var>.</li>
          <li>
            Let <var>interval distance</var> be the result of evaluating
            <code>(<var>time fraction</var> - <var>start offset</var>) /
                  (<var>end offset</var> - <var>start offset</var>)</code>
          </li>
          <li>
            Return the result of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-interpolation" title="interpolation">interpolating</a>
            between the property values defined for <var>start keyframe</var>
            and <var>end keyframe</var> using the procedure defined for their
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-property-type">property type</a> with <var>interval distance</var> as the
            interpolation parameter.
          </li>
        </ol>
        <div class="note">
          <p>Note that this procedure assumes the following about the list of
             <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> specified on the effect:</p>
          <ul>
            <li>Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> has a specified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset</a> in
                the range [0, 1].
            </li><li>The list of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> is sorted in ascending order by
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional
                offset</a>.
            </li><li>Each specified property value is a valid and supported value.
            </li><li>For a given property, there is a most one specified property
                value on each keyframe.
          </li></ul>
          <p>
            It is the responsibility of the user of the model (for example,
            a declarative markup or programming interface) to ensure these
            conditions are met.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p class="note">
          Note that this procedure permits overlapping <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a>.
          The behavior is that at the point of overlap the output value jumps to
          the value of last defined <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> at that offset.
          For overlapping frames at 0 or 1, the output value for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction" title="time fraction">time fractions</a> less than 0 or greater than
          or equal to 1 is the value of the first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> or the last
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>keyframes</var> respectively.
        </p>
        <div class="issue">
          <p>
            In the presence of certain timing functions, the input time
            fraction to an animation effect is not limited to the range [0, 1].
            Currently, however, keyframe offsets are limited to the range
            [0, 1] and property values are simply extrapolated for input time
            fractions outside this range. We are considering removing this
            restriction for the following reasons.
          </p>
          <p>
            We are considering removing the restriction since cases exist where
            it is useful to be able to specify non-linear changes in property
            values at time fractions outside the range [0, 1].
          </p>
          <p>
            While this effect could be achieved by careful modification of the
            timing function, this approach is complex and breaks the model's
            separation of timing concerns from animation effects. An example is
            an animation which is subject to an 'overshoot' timing function and
            which has an effect that sweeps through a non-linear color space.
          </p>
          <p>
            See <a href="http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/public-fx/2013AprJun/0184.html">section
            4 (Keyframe offsets outside [0, 1]) of minuted discussion from Tokyo
              2013 F2F</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="procedure-for-evenly-distributing-keyframes">              
        <h4><span class="secno">4.3.2 </span>Procedure for evenly distributing keyframes</h4>
        <p>
          Whilst the Web Animations model assumes a sorted list of
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> with specified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offsets</a> in the
          range [0, 1] many users of the model require a facility for
          automatically distributing keyframes when positional offsets are not
          provided.
          A procedure for evenly distributing keyframes with unspecified
          positional offsets is provided below.
        </p>
        <p>
          Given a list of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> whose <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offets</a> are
          either a real number in the range [0, 1] or unspecified,
          we define such as list as <dfn id="dfn-loosely-sorted-by-offset">loosely sorted by offset</dfn> if, for
          each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in the list that has a specified offset, the
          offset is greater than or equal to the offset of the previous
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in the list with a specified offset, if any.
        </p>
        <p>
          Given a list of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a>, <var>initial keyframe list</var>,
          that is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-loosely-sorted-by-offset">loosely sorted by offset</a> we can evenly distribute the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> with unspecified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offsets</a> between
          those frames with specified offsets using the following procedure:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Let <var>distributed keyframes</var> be a copy of <var>initial
              keyframe list</var>.
          </li><li>If there is no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>distributed keyframes</var>
              with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional
              offset</a> of 0, then,
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If there is more than one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>distributed
                  keyframes</var> and the first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> does not have
                  a specified positional offset,</dt>
              <dd>
                Set the positional offset of the first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in
                <var>distributed keyframes</var> to 0.
              </dd>
              <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
              <dd>
                Temporarily add an empty <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> to the
                start of <var>distributed keyframes with a positional
                offset of 0.
              </var></dd>
            </dl>
          </li><li>Likewise, if there is no <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in <var>distributed
              keyframes</var> with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset</a> of
              1, then,
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If <var>distributed keyframes</var> is not empty and the last
                  <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> does not have a specified positional
                  offset,</dt>
              <dd>
                Set the positional offset of the last <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> in
                <var>distributed keyframes</var> to 1.
              </dd>
              <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
              <dd>
                Temporarily append an empty <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> to the end of
                <var>distributed keyframes with a positional offset of 1.
              </var></dd>
            </dl>
          </li><li>Set the offset of all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> in <var>distributed
              keyframes</var> without a specified <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-positional-offset-of-a-keyframe" title="positional offset of a keyframe">positional offset</a> as
              so that for a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a>, <var>k</var>, without a specified
              offset, if:
              <ul>
                <li><var>a</var> is the positional offset of the last
                    <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a specified offset appearing in
                    <var>distributed keyframes</var> before <var>k</var>,
                </li><li><var>b</var> is the positional offset of the first
                    <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> with a specified offset appearing in
                    <var>pre-processed keyframes</var> after <var>k</var>,
                </li><li><var>n</var> is the number of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> between
                    <var>a</var> and <var>b</var>, and
                </li><li><var>i</var> is the index of <var>k</var> among the
                    <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframes</a> between <var>a</var> and <var>b</var>
                    such that the first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> has index 1 and the last
                    <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-keyframe">keyframe</a> has index <var>n</var>;
              </li></ul>
              <p>
                then the offset of <var>k</var> is
                <code><var>a</var> + (<var>b</var> - <var>a</var>)
                * <var>i</var>
                / (<var>n</var> + 1)</code>
              </p>
          </li><li>If any temporary keyframes were added to <var>distributed
              keyframes</var> in steps 1 or 2, remove them from <var>distributed
              keyframes</var>.
          </li><li>Return <var>distributed keyframes</var>.
        </li></ol>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="path-animation-effects">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.4 </span>Path animation effects</h3>
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation effect</dfn> is an <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a> that
        produces transform <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation values</a>
        such that a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-element">target element</a> follows a specified geometric curve.
      </p>
      <p>
        The <dfn id="dfn-path">path</dfn> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation effect</a> is provided by an
        SVG Path, as defined in SVG [<cite><a href="#bib-SVG112" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SVG112</a></cite>].
        A <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path">path</a> consists of a list of <dfn id="dfn-path-elements">path elements</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The <dfn id="dfn-automatic-rotation-flag">automatic rotation flag</dfn> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation
        effect</a>, if set, specifies that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation
        value</a> generated by the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation effect</a> produces
        a rotation that matches the directional tangent vector of the
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path">path</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        The <dfn id="dfn-rotation-angle">rotation angle</dfn> parameter of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation
        effect</a> specifies a constant rotation that applies to the target
        transform in addition to any rotation generated by setting the
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-automatic-rotation-flag">automatic rotation flag</a>.
      </p>
      <p>
        Each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation effect</a> has an associated <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation">composition
        operation</a> that specifies whether the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation
        values</a> generated by the effect <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-replace" title="composition operation replace">replace</a> the underlying value
        or <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-add" title="composition operation add">add</a> to it.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="the-unaccumulated-animation-value-of-a-path-animation-effect">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.4.1 </span>The unaccumulated animation value of a path animation effect</h4>
        <p>
          The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-path-animation-effect">path animation
          effect</a> for a given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time fraction</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying
          value</a> is given by the following process:
          </p><ol>
            <li>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-element-fraction">element fraction</a>
              are calculated by applying the process defined in 
              <a href="#calculating-the-current-element-and-element-fraction" class="sectionRef">section 4.4.2 Calculating the current element and element fraction</a>.
            </li>
            <li>
              The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-value">rotation value</a> is calculated by applying
              the process defined in 
              <a href="#calculating-the-rotation-value-of-the-current-element" class="sectionRef">section 4.4.3 Calculating the rotation value of the current element</a>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Let <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-translation-value">translation value</a> is calculated by 
              applying the process defined in
              <a href="#calculating-the-translation-value-of-the-current-element" class="sectionRef">section 4.4.4 Calculating the translation value of the current element</a>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Let the <var>transform value</var> be the result of combining
              the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-value">rotation value</a> and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-translation-value"> translation value</a>
              by constructing a transform list consisting of the
              translation value followed by the rotation value.
            </li>
            <li>
              If the <a title="operation">composition operation</a> is 
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-composition-operation-replace" title="composition operation replace">replace</a>, then the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> of the effect is the
              <var>transform value</var>.
            </li>
            <li>
              Otherwise, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unaccumulated-animation-value">unaccumulated animation value</a> of the 
              effect is the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-underlying-value">underlying value</a> accumulated with the
              <var>transform value</var> according to the process defined in
              <a href="#the--transform-function--type" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.2.7 The &lt;transform-function&gt; type</a>.
            </li>
          </ol>
        <p></p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-current-element-and-element-fraction">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.4.2 </span>Calculating the current element and element fraction</h4>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            Each element in the path (excluding moveto elements) is allocated
            an equally sized non-overlapping segment, with segments 
            collectively partitioning the range [0, 1].
          </p>
          <p>
            The <var>current element</var> is the <a>path element</a>
            corresponding to the <a>current time fraction</a>. The
            <var>element fraction</var> represents the offset into the
            <var>current element</var> at the <a>current time fraction</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-current-element">current element</dfn> and <dfn id="dfn-element-fraction">element fraction</dfn> are
          determined using the following procedure:
        </p>
        <dl class="switch">
          <dt>
            If the <a>current time fraction</a> is greater than or equal to 1
          </dt>
          <dd>
            the <var>current element</var> is the last element in the path,
            and the <var>element fraction</var> is 1.
          </dd>
          <dt>
            If the <a>current time fraction</a> is less than 0
          </dt>
          <dd>
            the <var>current element</var> is the first element in the path,
            and the <var>element fraction</var> is 0.
          </dd>
          <dt>
            Otherwise
          </dt>
          <dd>
            <ol>
              <li>
                Let <var>effective element list</var> be a clone of the
                <a>element list</a> with all moveto elements removed.
              </li>
              <li>
                Let <var>time index</var> be the <a>current time fraction</a>
                multiplied by the number of elements in the <var>effective
                element list</var>.
              </li>
              <li>
                Let <var>current element</var> be the element in the
                <a>effective element list</a> at the index given by
                <code>floor(<var>time index</var>)</code>.
              </li>
              <li>
                Let <var>element fraction</var> be the value given by
                <code><var>time index</var> - floor(<var>time index</var>)
                </code>.
              </li>
            </ol>
          </dd>
        </dl>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-rotation-value-of-the-current-element">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.4.3 </span>Calculating the rotation value of the current element</h4>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-rotation-value">rotation value</dfn> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> is the
          rotation produced by that element at the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-element-fraction">element fraction</a>.
        </p>
        <dl class="switch">
          <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-automatic-rotation-flag">automatic rotation flag</a> is not set,</dt>
          <dd>
            the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-value">rotation value</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> is the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-angle">rotation angle</a>
          </dd>
          <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
          <dd>
            the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-value">rotation value</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> is the sum
            of:
            <ul>
              <li>
                the angle of the tangent vector of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a>
                at the point selected in
