                <a href="#calculating-the-translation-value-of-the-current-element" class="sectionRef">section 4.4.4 Calculating the translation value of the current element</a>
                for the purpose of calculating the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-translation-value">translation value</a>; 
                and
              </li>
              <li>
                the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-rotation-angle">rotation angle</a>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p>
          For continuous elements (all elements except moveto), the angle of
          the tangent vector for the purpose of these calculations is defined 
          to be an integer multiple of 2&#x3c0; different from the value given by
          standard mathematical formulae for tangents to curves in 2
          dimensional space. See 
          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tangential_angle">
          http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tangential_angle</a> for 
          more information.
        </p>
        <p>
          For moveto, which is discontinuous, the angle of the tangent vector
          for the purpose of these calculations is always an integer multiple
          of 2&#x3c0;.
        </p>
        <p>
          At non-smooth junction points, the angle of the tangent vector for
          the purpose of these calculations is determined by the tangent to
          the curve after the junction.
        </p>
        <p>
          The initial value of the angle of the tangent vector is computed 
          using the first element of the curve, and is always in the range
          [0, 2&#x3c0;).
        </p>
        <p>
          Single continuous path elements must never produce tangent
          vector angles that are discontinuous over their defined region. This
          implies that a single unique solution is available for all points on
          continuous path elements.
        </p>
        <p>
          When computing angles after discontinuous or non-smooth jumps,
          multiple possible solutions will be available -these solutions 
          differ by integer multiples of 2&#x3c0;. The solution that lies closest
          to the previous tangent angle must be selected.
        </p>
        <p>
          Please see
          <a href="#algorithms-for-path-animation-effects" class="sectionRef">section B. Algorithms for path animation effects</a>
          for a full non-normative treatment of this topic.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="calculating-the-translation-value-of-the-current-element">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.4.4 </span>Calculating the translation value of the current element</h4>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-translation-value">translation value</dfn> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> is
          determined using the following process:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>
            Let <var>length</var> be the length, in pixels, of the 
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a>
          </li>
          <li>
            Let <var>element distance</var> be equal to the formula
            <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-element-fraction">element fraction</a> &#xd7; <var>length</var></code>.
          </li>
          <li>
            Let <var>point</var> be the unique point along the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-element">current element</a> which is <var>element distance</var>
            along the path from the start of the path.
          </li>
          <li>
            The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-translation-value">translation value</a> is the translation transform
            that transforms the point at the start of the path to 
            <var>point</var>.
          </li>
        </ol>
        <p>
          The length of a path element is determined, where possible, via 
          closed-form solutions. For some path elements (e.g. beziers) a
          closed-form solution is not generally possible, and approximations
          should be used.
        </p>
        <p>
          The length of a moveto element is always 0.
        </p>
        <p>
          Please see
          <a href="#algorithms-for-path-animation-effects" class="sectionRef">section B. Algorithms for path animation effects</a>
          for a full non-normative treatment of this topic.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="todo">
        <p>
          Need to describe how <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/css3-transforms/#transform-origin">transform-origin</a>
          is applied.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="animatable-properties">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.5 </span>Animatable properties</h3>
      <div class="section" id="css-properties">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.5.1 </span>CSS Properties</h4>
        <p>
          Unless specified otherwise, all CSS properties should be considered
          animatable. Examples of properties which are explicitly marked as not
          animatable are those defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] and
          [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-ANIMATIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-ANIMATIONS</a></cite>].
        </p>
        <div class="note">
          <p>
            [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] requires future CSS specifications to provide
            an &#x2018;animatable:&#x2019; line for each newly defined property.
            This line defines whether properties can animate and how that
            animation occurs. Note that &#x2018;animatable: none&#x2019; in this
            regard merely means that a property is not continuously animatable
            - that is, not interpolable.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            Animation and Transition properties are not animatable. As defined
            in <a href="#target-properties" class="sectionRef">section 4.1.1 Target properties</a> specifying
            these properties as part of an animation effect will not result in
            any changes to the target element. This restriction prevents
            self-modifying animations.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="note">
          <p>
            Properties defined as animatable by CSS Transitions in
            [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] specify animation types. These types in turn
            specify interpolation procedures for each property. The procedures
            described in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] are replaced by the interpolation
            definitions in <a href="#animation-of-property-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6 Animation of property types</a>. Note that this change is
            backwards-compatible - the interpolation definitions in this
            specification produce the same result as [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>]
            unless [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] specifies that no interpolation can
            occur.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            The mechanism of action of [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] and this
            specification sometimes differ. However, the results of both
            mechanisms are consistent with each other.
          </p>
          <p>
            For example, [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] length values are always
            converted to computed style pixel lengths and interpolated as
            numbers, whereas this specification performs interpolation between
            different length units using calc expressions.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          <a href="#animation-of-property-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6 Animation of property types</a>
          defines how pairs of CSS values are interpolated, as well as how
          two values add together.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="css-properties-defined-by-svg">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.5.2 </span>CSS Properties defined by SVG</h4>
        <p>
          All CSS properties defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-SVG112" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SVG112</a></cite>] are animatable except where
          explicitly marked otherwise. Where SVG types take CSS values, this
          specification defines how those values interpolate and add together.
          For all other values, interpolation and addition is defined by
          [<cite><a href="#bib-SVG112" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">SVG112</a></cite>].
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="svg-attributes">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.5.3 </span>SVG Attributes</h4>
        <p>
          There are a number of SVG attributes which do not map to CSS
          properties which are nevertheless animatable. The procedures for
          animating these attributes are defined in <b>TBD</b>.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="animation-of-property-types">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.6 </span>Animation of property types</h3>
      <div class="section">
        <p>
          When animating property types, procedures for interpolation and
          addition are required.
        </p>
        <p>
          [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-VALUES" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-VALUES</a></cite>] defines common values and units that CSS 
          properties accept.
        </p>
        <p>
          To determine the appropriate animation interpolation and addition
          algorithms to use for any given start and end value, first determine
          the types of the values. If the types match, then the algorithms used
          are given by <a href="#animation-of-like-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.2 Animation of like types</a>. 
        </p>
        <p>
          Some properties accept values of multiple different primitive types.
          For example, the padding-* properties accept a type of
          <code>&lt;padding-width&gt;</code>, which can either be a
          <code>&lt;length&gt;</code> or a <code>&lt;percentage&gt;</code>. <a href="#animation-of-non-matching-primitive-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.3 Animation of non-matching primitive types</a> defines the algorithm to be used to deal with
          interpolation when the type of the start and the type of the end do
          not match.
        </p>
        <p>
          Some properties accept a combination of typed values and keywords.
          For example, border-width accepts both <code>&lt;length&gt;</code>
          values and &#x2018;thick&#x2019;, &#x2018;medium&#x2019; and
          &#x2018;thin&#x2019; keywords. <a href="#animation-of-keywords-and-primitive-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.4 Animation of keywords and primitive types</a> describes how to deal with interpolation to
          and/or from a keyword value.
        </p>
        <p>
          <a href="#animation-of-shorthand-properties" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.5 Animation of shorthand properties</a>
          describes how to deal with interpolation between CSS shorthand values.
        </p>
        <p>
          Calc expressions can be used in place of <code>&lt;length&gt;</code>,
          <code>&lt;frequency&gt;</code>, <code>&lt;angle&gt;</code>,
          <code>&lt;time&gt;</code>, <code>&lt;number&gt;</code> and
          <code>&lt;integer&gt;</code> values. <a href="#animation-of-css-calc-expressions" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.6 Animation of CSS calc expressions</a>
          describes how to deal with interpolation to and/or from calc
          expressions.
        </p>
        <p>
          <a href="#animation-of-transform-lists" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.7 Animation of transform lists</a>
          describes how to deal with interpolation of CSS and SVG transform
          lists.
        </p>
        <p>
          If no specific algorithms are provided here, then the default 
          algorithms defined in 
          <a href="#default-animation-algorithms" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.1 Default Animation Algorithms</a> 
          are used.  Note that the neutral value does not match any value 
          type and thus all calculations involving the neutral value will 
          use the default algorithms.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="default-animation-algorithms">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.1 </span>Default Animation Algorithms</h4>
        <p>
        Given the output <i>p</i> of a timing function, the result
        <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> of interpolating between two values,
        <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> and <i>V</i><sub>end</sub> is given by
         </p><blockquote>
          <dl class="switch">
            <dt>If 0 &lt;= <i>p</i> &lt; 0.5</dt>
            <dd><i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = <i>V</i><sub>start</sub></dd>
            <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
            <dd><i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = <i>V</i><sub>end</sub></dd>
          </dl>
         </blockquote>
         Note that interpolation is never performed on invalid values.
        <p></p>
        <p>
          Addition is between two values <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> and 
          <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>. The result <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> is given by 
         </p><blockquote>
            <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> + <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> 
         </blockquote>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-like-types">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.2 </span>Animation of like types</h4>
        <p>
          If the result of the interpolation is specified by a calc expression
          and the units of <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> and <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>
          are related by a constant scalar multiple then the result is
          evaluated as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-VALUES" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-VALUES</a></cite>] before being returned.
          </p><div class="annotation">
            The CSS &#x2018;px&#x2019; unit is related to the CSS &#x2018;in&#x2019;
            unit by a constant scalar multiple of 96 (i.e. 96px = 1in). On the
            other hand, the CSS &#x2018;em&#x2019; unit is not related to the
            &#x2018;in&#x2019; unit by a constant scalar multiple.
          </div>
          <div class="note">
            [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>] defines the following default formula for interpolation:
            <blockquote>
              <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = (1 - <i>p</i>) * <i>V</i><sub>start</sub>
                + <i>p</i>  * <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>
            </blockquote>
          </div>
        <p></p>
        <p>
          If the result of the addition is specified by a calc expression and
          the units of <i>V</i><sub>a</sub>  and <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>  are
          related by a constant scalar multiple then the result is evaluated as
          defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-VALUES" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-VALUES</a></cite>] before being returned.
          </p><div class="note">
            The default formula for single valued types is to use the CSS3
            calc() function: 
            <blockquote>
              <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc(<i>V</i><sub>a</sub> + 
              <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>)
            </blockquote>
          </div>
        <p></p>
        <div class="section" id="the--integer----number--and--percentage---------------types">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.1 </span>
            The &lt;integer&gt;, &lt;number&gt; and &lt;percentage&gt; 
            types
          </h5>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>].
          </p>
          <p>
            Addition is performed as <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = 
            <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> + <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--length----angle----time--and---------------frequency--types">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.2 </span>
            The &lt;length&gt;, &lt;angle&gt;, &lt;time&gt; and 
            &lt;frequency&gt; types
          </h5>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed as <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = (1 - 
            <i>p</i>) * <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> + <i>p</i>  * <i>V</i>
            <sub>end</sub>.
          </p>
          <p>
            Addition is performed as <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc(<i>V</i>
            <sub>a</sub> + <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>).
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--resolution--type">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.3 </span>The &lt;resolution&gt; type</h5>
          <div class="issue">Do we want to interpolate this?</div>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed as <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = 
            (1 - <i>p</i>) * <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> + <i>p</i>  * 
            <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>.
          </p>
          <p>
            Addition is performed as <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = 
            calc(<i>V</i><sub>a</sub> + <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>).
          </p>        
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--color--type">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.4 </span>The &lt;color&gt; type</h5>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>].
          </p>
          <p>
            Addition is performed on each RGBA color component in premultiplied
            space, clamping so it is within the range specified in 
            [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3COLOR" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3COLOR</a></cite>].
          </p>
          <div class="issue">
            What we do for addition depends on why we're adding. As defined
            here, the result will tend to saturate to opaque white.
          </div>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--image--type">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.5 </span>The &lt;image&gt; type</h5>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed using the cross-fade() function as
            defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS4IMAGES" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS4IMAGES</a></cite>]:
            </p><blockquote>
              <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = cross-fade(<i>p</i>,
              <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> , <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>).
            </blockquote>
          <p></p>
          <p>
            Addition is defined as the composition of <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> over
            <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>,, with <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> and
            <i>V</i><sub>b</sub> aligned at their top left corners. The height
            and width of the result is the maximum of the heights and widths of
            <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> and <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>. Any result pixels
            outside the bounds of <i>V</i><sub>a</sub> or <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>
            are defined to be rgba(0, 0, 0, 0).
          </p>
          <div class="issue">
            This does not match the saturating behaviour defined for addition 
            of colors.
          </div>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--position--type">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.6 </span>The &lt;position&gt; type</h5>
          <p>
            Before interpolation or addition, any shorthand is expanded as
            described in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS21" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS21</a></cite>] to include both horizontal and vertical
            positions. Keywords are converted to their equivalent percentage
            values as described in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS21" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS21</a></cite>].
          </p>
          <p>
            Interpolation or addition is performed on each provided value in
            accordance with its type.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="the--transform-function--type">
          <h5><span class="secno">4.6.2.7 </span>The &lt;transform-function&gt; type</h5>
          <p>
            Interpolation is performed as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSFORMS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSFORMS</a></cite>].
          </p>
          <p>
            Addition is performed as an accumulation as defined in 
            [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSFORMS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSFORMS</a></cite>].
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-non-matching-primitive-types">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.3 </span>Animation of non-matching primitive types</h4>
        <p>
          In general, non-matching primitive types cannot be interpolated or
          added. Non-matching primitive types may only be interpolated or added
          if the property value they are defined on allows both those types,
          for example &lt;length&gt; and &lt;percent&gt;. In these cases, the CSS
          calc() function as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-VALUES" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-VALUES</a></cite>] is used.
        </p>
        <p>
          For interpolation:
          </p><blockquote>
            <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc((1 - <i>p</i>) * 
            <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> + <i>p</i>  * <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>).
          </blockquote>  
        <p></p>
        <p>
          For addition:
          </p><blockquote>
            <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc(<i>V</i><sub>a</sub> + <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>).
          </blockquote>
        <p></p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-keywords-and-primitive-types">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.4 </span>Animation of keywords and primitive types</h4>
        <p>
          A keyword value may be defined as equivalent to a primitive type,
          either directly, or via some intermediate calculation. For example,
          for the background-position property, [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS21" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS21</a></cite>] defines the
          &#x2018;top&#x2019; keyword to be equivalent to &#x2018;0%&#x2019;. In
          these cases, the equivalent primitive type shall be used, and
          interpolation and addition performed as defined in <a href="#animation-of-like-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.2 Animation of like types</a> or <a href="#animation-of-non-matching-primitive-types" class="sectionRef">section 4.6.3 Animation of non-matching primitive types</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          In the case that a keyword maps onto a finite ordered list of values
          with a determinable spacing between them, then a step-wise
          interpolation is used. For example, the font-weight property 
          accepts an ordered list of values from 100 to 900 in
          steps of 100. The interpolation in this case is defined as ((1 -
          <i>p</i>) * <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> + <i>p</i> *
          <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>), rounded to the nearest member of the list.
          Addition in this case is defined as (<i>V</i><sub>a</sub> +
          <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>), clamped to remain within the specifed list of
          values. 
        </p>
        <p>
          In all other cases, the keyword value is not interpolable. Result of
          add is the right hand side.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-shorthand-properties">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.5 </span>Animation of shorthand properties</h4>
        <p>
          Shorthand properties are animated as defined in [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSITIONS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSITIONS</a></cite>].
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-css-calc-expressions">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.6 </span>Animation of CSS calc expressions</h4>
        <p>
          For interpolation:
          </p><blockquote>
            <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc((1 - <i>p</i>) *
            <i>V</i><sub>start</sub> + <i>p</i>  * <i>V</i><sub>end</sub>).
          </blockquote>  
        <p></p>
        <p>
          For addition:
          </p><blockquote>
            <i>V</i><sub>res</sub> = calc(<i>V</i><sub>a</sub> +
            <i>V</i><sub>b</sub>).
          </blockquote>
        <p></p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="animation-of-transform-lists">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.6.7 </span>Animation of transform lists</h4>
        <p>
          Interpolation of transform lists is performed as defined in
          [<cite><a href="#bib-CSS3-TRANSFORMS" rel="biblioentry" class="bibref">CSS3-TRANSFORMS</a></cite>]
        </p>
        <p>
          Addition of transform lists is performed by appending
          <i>V</i><sub>b</sub> to <i>V</i><sub>a</sub>.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>

    <div class="section" id="custom-effects">
      <h3><span class="secno">4.7 </span>Custom effects</h3>
      <div class="informative informative-bg">
        <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
          In some situations the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a> provided by Web Animations may be insufficient.
          For example, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a>
          defined here are only able to target certain CSS properties and DOM
          attributes.
          They are unable, therefore, to modify the <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/SVG11/struct.html#__svg__SVGSVGElement__currentScale"><code>currentScale</code></a>
          property of an SVG element to smoothly zoom the viewport without
          affecting the document content.
        </p>
        <p>
          In such cases where the provided <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a> do not provide needed functionality, an effect defined by
          script may be used.
          Such <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effects</a> receive a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-fraction">time
          fraction</a> from the timing model and are responsible for producing
          the desired effect corresponding to the specified time.
        </p>
        <p>
          Using an effect defined in script it is possible to animate not only
          otherwise un-animatable attributes and properties, but potentially
          anything that is accessible via script, including even producing audio
          or creating vibrations.
        </p>
        <p>
          For example, using a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effect</a> that draws to a <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/html5/the-canvas-element.html#the-canvas-element"><code>canvas</code></a>
          element it is possible to produce a complex animated effect
          featuring patterns that may be difficult to create using CSS or
          SVG.
          Compared to using the <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/animation-timing/">WindowAnimationTiming</a>
          interface, this approach ensures the animation is frame-rate
          independent and can be paused, reversed, eased with timing effects,
          accelerated, synchronized with other animations, and be controlled
          in the same manner as any other Web Animations animation without any
          additional programming.
        </p>
      </div> <!-- informative -->
      <p>
        A <dfn id="dfn-custom-effect">custom effect</dfn> is an author-defined programming callback
        that is passed timing information whenever a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sample">sample</a> is performed.
      </p>
      <div class="section" id="execution-order-of-custom-effects">
        <h4><span class="secno">4.7.1 </span>Execution order of custom effects</h4>
        <p>
          Since <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effects</a>, unlike <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect" title="animation effect">animation effects</a>, are not limited to
          a single <a>target property</a> and the steps for assessing their
          order of execution differs from <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation
          effects</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">Custom effects</a> are executed after all
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a> have completed and
          applied their result to their targets (see <a href="#combining-with-other-styles--the-override-stylesheet" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.4 Combining with other styles: the override stylesheet</a>).
        </p>
        <p class="issue">
          Need to define this more precisely.
          Are styles flushed?
          Presumably they are.
          Can we suspend reflow for the duration of executing the script-based
          animation effects and just do it once afterwards?
        </p>
        <p>
          Within the set of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effects</a>, the
          order of execution is initially the same as that defined for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect" title="animation effect">animation effects</a> in <a href="#the-animation-stack" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.1 The animation stack</a>.
          However, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effects</a> may also override
          this ordering through a <dfn id="dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</dfn> property associated with
          the effect.
          This <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</a> property, if
          defined, specifies the order in which the callbacks are executed
          such that the callback of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effect</a> with the least
          priority is executed first.
        </p>
        <p>
          In deciding which of two <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect">custom effects</a>,
          <var>A</var> and <var>B</var>, should be executed first, the following
          rules are applied.
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> based on their
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</a> properties such
              that lower priorities are sorted first.
              If either does not have a defined <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</a>, then treat the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</a> as being zero for the
              purposes of sorting.</li>
          <li>If <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> have the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-custom-effect-priority" title="custom effect priority">priority</a>,
              sort <var>A</var> and <var>B</var> using the procedure defined for
              sorting <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effects</a> in <a href="#the-animation-stack" class="sectionRef">section 4.2.1 The animation stack</a>.</li>
        </ol>
        <p>
          Items sorted earlier are executed before those sorted later.
        </p>
      </div>
    </div>
    </div> <!-- End of animation model -->

    <div class="section" id="timing-events">
      <!--OddPage--><h2><span class="secno">5. </span>Timing events</h2>
      <div class="issue">
        Possibly move this section into <a href="#timing-model" class="sectionRef">section 3. Timing model</a>.
      </div>
      <div class="issue">
      <p>
        The current event model has two undesirable consequences:
        </p><ul>
          <li>
            Applications that need good-quality information on events will
            need to implement both seeked mode handling and normal mode
            handling. Having both is likely to result in applications only
            relying on the information available in the lower-quality
            seeked mode, as switching between the two is system-dependent,
            opaque to users of the model, and uncontrollable. This makes the
            higher-quality mode seem to be a complication rather than an
            improvement.
          </li>
          <li>
            Uneased timing can cause events to be reordered with respect
            to how they are visually percieved; and can also cause events
            to be delivered with timestamps in the future. This is likely to
            be quite confusing to users of the model.
          </li>
        </ul>
      <p></p>
      <p>
        We've explored a few different models to try and mitigate these
        problems. Some ideas we've looked at that seem promising:
        </p><ul>
          <li>
            Primitive onstart / onend events that fire only when an 
            animation first starts playing and last stops playing.
          </li>
          <li>
            An onchange event that fires when the play state (e.g. current
            iteration, fill state, etc.) of an Animation changes, and provides
            a summary only of ther changes since the last sample. This is 
            guaranteed to generate no more than one event per animation per
            sample.
          </li>
          <li>
            A lazily-constructed list of change elements that provides a more
            detailed understanding of the changes since the last sample. This
            would be somewhat costly to generate for large sample intervals,
            but would not be constructed by default.
          </li>
        </ul>
        <p>
          See <a href="http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/public-fx/2013AprJun/0184.html">
          Sections 8 and 14 of minuted discussion</a>.
        </p>
      <p></p>
      </div>
      <p>
        As <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a> play they report changes to
        their status through <dfn id="dfn-timing-event" title="timing event">timing events</dfn>.
      </p>
      <p>
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">Timing events</a> are a property of the Web
        Animations timing model.
        As a result they are dispatched even for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation" title="animation">animations</a> that do not have an associated
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation-effect">animation effect</a>, for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">animations</a> whose
        <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-target-element">target element</a> is not rendered because it or a parent element has
        <span class="property">display</span> property of <span class="prop-value">none</span>, and for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
        items</a> that perform no animation such as <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a>.
      </p>
      <div class="annotation">
        <p><strong>Relationship to CSS and SVG events</strong></p>
        <p>
          CSS defines <code>AnimationEvent</code>s and
          <code>TransitionEvent</code>s and SVG defines <code>TimeEvent</code>s.
          The proposal here is to dispatch <a class="idlType" href="#idl-def-TimingEvent"><code>TimingEvent</code></a>s in parallel to
          these events.
        </p>
        <p>
          A key difference is that the target of a <a class="idlType" href="#idl-def-TimingEvent"><code>TimingEvent</code></a> is a
          <a class="idlType" href="#idl-def-TimedItem"><code>TimedItem</code></a> and not content.
          This model leaves firing of events at content up to the declarative
          mapping onto the model (e.g. CSS or SVG).
          This approach makes the Web Animations model more self-contained
          whilst permitting different mappings for different markup.
          For example, CSS fires events at the target element whilst SVG fires
          events at the element that generated the animation.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="types-of-timing-events">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.1 </span>Types of timing events</h3>
          <dl>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-timingstart">timingstart</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Occurs at the moment when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> enters its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active
              interval</a> (from either direction).
            </p>
            <p>
              Note that if the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> starts a new
              iteration, this is treated as if this element momentarily exited
              its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> (producing a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingend">timingend</a>
              event), and entered it again (producing a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingstart">timingstart</a>
              event).
            </p>
            <ul>
              <li>Bubbles: yes</li>
              <li>Cancelable: no</li>
              <li>Context Info: localTime, documentTime, iterationIndex,
                                seeked</li>
            </ul>
          </dd>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Occurs at the moment when a <a href="#repeating">repeating</a>
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> changes value
              excluding changes to and from <code>null</code>.
            </p>
            <p>
              Note that if the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing group</a> starts a new
              iteration, this is treated as if this element momentarily exited
              its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> (causing the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>
              to become <code>null</code>), and entered it again (producing
              a new value for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a>) and hence producing no
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</a> event since the only changes to <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current
              iteration</a> are to and from <code>null</code>.
            </p>
            <ul>
              <li>Bubbles: yes</li>
              <li>Cancelable: no</li>
              <li>Context Info: localTime, documentTime, iterationIndex,
                                seeked</li>
            </ul>
          </dd>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-timingend">timingend</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Occurs at the moment when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> leaves its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active
              interval</a> (from either direction).
            </p>
            <ul>
              <li>Bubbles: yes</li>
              <li>Cancelable: no</li>
              <li>Context Info: localTime, documentTime, iterationIndex,
                                seeked</li>
            </ul>
          </dd>
          <dt><dfn id="dfn-timingcancel">timingcancel</dfn></dt>
          <dd>
            <p>
              Occurs when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> loses its association with
              a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
            </p>
            <ul>
              <li>Bubbles: yes</li>
              <li>Cancelable: no</li>
              <li>Context Info: None</li>
            </ul>
          </dd>
        </dl>
        <p class="issue">
          Can we rename these to just <em>start</em>, <em>iteration</em>,
          <em>end</em>, and <em>cancel</em>?
          They are only fired at <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a>, never
          DOM nodes, so they won't clash with other events.
          Is that enough or do the names need to be globally unique?
        </p>
        <div class="annotation">
          <p>
            Other potential event types for a later version:
          </p>
          <ul>
            <li><em>timingpause</em> &#x2014;
              fired whenever <code>paused</code> is newly true on the associated
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
              <p>
                Use case: show a graphic overlay to mark a cartoon as
                paused.<br> Likewise <em>unpause</em>.
              </p>
            </li>
            <li><em>timingseek</em> &#x2014;
              fired whenever <code>currentTime</code> is set on the
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>.
              <p>
                Use case: If you are implementing something like SVG's syncbase
                timing with script you often need to do some bookkeeping on
                a seek.
              </p>
            </li>
            <li><em>timingdirectionchange</em> &#x2014;
              fired whenever the effective direction of the item changes (due to
              the direction attribute, changes to playbackRate, calling reverse
              etc. on either the item or an ancestor)
              <p>
                Use case: update UI to represent rewinding;
                stop audio when playing backwards.
              </p>
            </li>
            <li><em>timingnewanimation</em> &#x2014;
              fired whenever a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-animation">Animation</a> object is created.
              <p>
                Use case: a timeline debugger. You want to show all animations
                that are playing or yet-to-play.
                Using this event (and
                <code>document.timeline.getCurrentAnimations</code>) you could
                build up a timegraph.
              </p>
              <p>
                I think this sort of event and this sort of use case would fit
                the MutationObserver pattern well.
                We could introduce a whole class of mutation records targetted
                at debugging (e.g. <em>timereschedule</em>)
              </p>
          </li></ul>
          <p>
            Also, although this is a bit different to a regular event (since
            it's qualified by a parameter), it seems like it might be nice to be
            able to do something like:
          </p>
          <pre class="example sh_javascript sh_sourceCode">anim<span class="sh_symbol">.</span><span class="sh_function">onprogress</span><span class="sh_symbol">(</span><span class="sh_number">0.8</span><span class="sh_symbol">,</span>
 <span class="sh_keyword">function</span><span class="sh_symbol">()</span> <span class="sh_cbracket">{</span>
  <span class="sh_comment">// Issue a request to prefetch the next episode</span>
 <span class="sh_cbracket">}</span><span class="sh_symbol">);</span></pre>
          <p>
            It would be called whenever you got a sample where
            <code>(<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-time">active time</a> / <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a>)</code> &#x2265;
            <var>progress</var> was newly true.
          </p>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="uneased-timing">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.2 </span>Uneased timing</h3>
        <div class="informative informative-bg">
          <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">Timing events</a> in Web Animations rely on
            a mode of operating the timing model that does not apply <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function" title="timing function">timing functions</a> called <em>uneased
            timing</em>.
            There are two reasons for this:
          </p>
          <ul>
            <li>
              <p>
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">Timing functions</a> are not always invertible.
              </p>
              <p>
                In order to dispatch events in the correct order it is often
                necessary to convert from a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-local-time">local
                time</a> to a common time space for sorting and non-invertible
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing functions</a> make this
                impractical.
              </p>
            </li>
            <li>
              <p>
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">Timing functions</a> on parent <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group" title="timing group">timing groups</a> can cause unnecessary
                events to be generated.
              </p>
              <p>
                For example, consider a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> that has a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">timing
                function</a> that is not monotonically increasing such as
                a bounce effect.
                Within a single iteration of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> child <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item" title="timed item">timed items</a> may repeatedly exit and enter
                their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a>.
                Dispatching a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing event</a> on each such moment is
                unlikely to be useful to most applications.
              </p>
            </li>
          </ul>
          <p>
            An analogue is a graphics editing program where the user can apply
            a blur filter to a geometric shape.
            The graphics program may draw a selection box around the bounding
            box of the geometric shape ignoring the fact that the blur stretches
            (infinitely) beyond the selection box.
          </p>
          <p>
            Furthermore, since <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill modes</a> affect the
            calculation of times in ways that obscure the boundaries of the
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-interval">active interval</a> they are also ignored when operating in
            <em>uneased time</em>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-uneased-timing">uneased timing</dfn> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> refers to
          performing any of the calculations defined for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
          with the following exceptions:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function">Timing functions</a> on the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
              item</a> and all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a> are
              ignored.</li>
          <li>The <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-fill-mode">fill modes</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
              and all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a> are
              treated as <span class="prop-value">none.</span></li>
        </ul>
        <p>
          For example, the <em>uneased inherited time</em> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          item</a> is calculated using the regular definition of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-inherited-time">inherited
          time</a> after applying the two modifications to the timing of the
          item and its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestors</a> noted above.
        </p>
        <p>
          Normally the time value used as input to a child <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
          of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a> is the group's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-transformed-time">transformed time</a>.
          However, since <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-timing">uneased timing</a> does not apply <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-function" title="timing function">timing functions</a>, we refer to <dfn id="dfn-uneased-child-time">uneased
          child time</dfn> which is equivalent to both <em>uneased transformed
          time</em> and <em>uneased directed time</em>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="inverse-timing-calculations">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.3 </span>Inverse timing calculations</h3>
        <p>
          For times calculated using <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-timing">uneased timing</a> it is possible to
          perform the reverse operation to, for example, convert times from
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed item</a> to that of its its <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing
          group</a> or <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          Calculating the <dfn id="dfn-uneased-local-time-from-uneased-child-time"><em>uneased local time</em> from <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-child-time">uneased child
          time</a></dfn> of a given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> requires recording the
          iteration index that corresponds to the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-child-time">uneased child time</a> and
          is calculated as follows.
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li>Let <var>item</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> for which the
              <em>uneased local time</em> is to be calculated.</li>
          <li>Let <var>child time</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-child-time">uneased child time</a> to be
              converted.</li>
          <li>Let <var>iteration index</var> be the value of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current
              iteration</a> corresponding to <var>child time</var>.</li>
          <li>Calculate the <var>current direction</var> of <var>item</var>
              using the procedure defined in <a href="#calculating-the-directed-time" class="sectionRef">section 3.11.1 Calculating the directed time</a> substituting <var>iteration index</var>
              for the <em>current iteration</em>.</li>
          <li>
            <p>
              Let the <var>uneased iteration time</var> be the result
              corresponding to the first matching condition from below.
            </p>
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If the <var>current direction is <em>forwards</em>,</var></dt>
              <dd>
                <var>child time</var>
              </dd>
              <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
              <dd>
                <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> - <var>child time</var></code>
              </dd>
            </dl>
          </li>
          <li>
            <p>
              Let the <var>uneased scaled active time</var> be the result
              corresponding to the first matching condition from below.
            </p>
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> is zero,</dt>
              <dd>
                zero
              </dd>
              <dt>If <var>uneased iteration time</var> equals <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration
                  duration</a>,</dt>
              <dd>
                <code><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-repeated-duration">repeated duration</a> * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start offset</a></code>
              </dd>
              <dt>Otherwise,</dt>
              <dd>
                <code><var>iteration index</var> * <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a>
                + <var>uneased iteration time</var></code>
              </dd>
            </dl>
          </li>
          <li>
            <p>
              Let the <var>uneased active time</var> be the result corresponding
              to the first matching condition from below.
            </p>
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
                  is zero,</dt>
              <dd>
                positive infinity unless <var>scaled active time</var> is zero,
                in which case the <var>active time is zero
              </var></dd>
              <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback rate</a>
                  is positive,</dt>
              <dd>
                <code>(<var>uneased scaled active time</var> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start
                offset</a>) / <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback
                rate</a></code>
              </dd>
              <dt>Otherwise,
              </dt><dd>
                <code>(<var>uneased scaled active time</var> - <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-offset">start
                offset</a>) / <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item-playback-rate" title="timed item playback rate">playback
                rate</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active-duration">active duration</a></code>
              </dd>
          </dl></li>
          <li>Return <code><var>uneased active time</var> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-start-delay">start
              delay</a></code>.
          </li>
        </ol>
        <p>
          Note that the above procedure is only defined when the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-uneased-child-time">uneased
          child time</a> is defined, that is, not <code>null</code>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-uneased-inherited-time-from-uneased-local-time"><em>uneased inherited time</em> from <em>uneased local
          time</em></dfn> is simply the sum of the <em>uneased local time</em>
          and the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item" title="timed item">start time</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-timeline-time-from-the-current-time-of-a-player"><em><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> time</em> from the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> of
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a></dfn> is calculated as follows.
        </p>
        <blockquote>
          <code><var>timeline time</var> =
            (<a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current time</a> + <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-drift">time drift</a>) /
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">playback rate</a> +
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-start-time" title="player start time">start time</a></code>
        </blockquote>
        <p>
          If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player-playback-rate" title="player playback rate">player's playback rate</a> is
          zero, the <var>timeline time</var> is undefined.
          The handling of an undefined value depends on the context in which it
          is used.
          Typically, a current <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> for the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is
          available and this is used in place of the undefined value.
        </p>
        <p>
          Provided that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> values used when
          calculating the <em>uneased local time</em> are recorded, it is
          possible, by applying the above definitions in succession, to
          calculate the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> corresponding to
          the <em>uneased local time</em> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> associated with
          that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="event-parameters">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.4 </span>Event parameters</h3>
        <p>
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">Timing events</a> have an associated <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-local-time">event
          local time</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-iteration-index">event iteration
          index</a>, and <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-dispatch-flag">seeked dispatch flag</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-event-local-time">event local time</dfn> is the <em>uneased local time</em> of
          the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> that generated event at the moment the event is
          scheduled to occur.
          This time is constrained by the timing of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent timing
          group</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-interval">iteration interval</a> such that when converted to an
          <em>uneased iteration time</em> in the parent's <a href="#iteration-time-space">iteration time space</a> (see <a href="#inverse-timing-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 5.3 Inverse timing calculations</a>) it lies
          within the range 0 &#x2264; <em>uneased iteration time</em> &#x2264;
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-iteration-duration">iteration duration</a> (of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group" title="parent timing
          group">parent</a>).
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</dfn> is the result of converting the
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-local-time">event local time</a> into the time space of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a>
          that sampled the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>.
          If is calculated using the procedures defined in <a href="#inverse-timing-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 5.3 Inverse timing calculations</a>.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-event-iteration-index">event iteration index</dfn> is the value of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
          item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> and moment the event is scheduled
          to occur.
        </p>
        <p>
          The <dfn id="dfn-seeked-dispatch-flag">seeked dispatch flag</dfn> is a boolean value set to
          <code>true</code> if this event was generated as a result of applying
          <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event dispatch</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="propagation-path">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.5 </span>Propagation path</h3>
        <p>
          The <a href="http://www.w3.org/TR/DOM-Level-3-Events/#glossary-propagation-path">propagation
          path</a> for a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing event</a> generated by <var>item</var>,
          is simply <var>item</var> itself.
        </p>
        <p class="note">
          Note that unlike <code>AnimationEvent</code>s and
          <code>TransitionEvent</code>s in CSS, and <code>TimeEvent</code>s in
          SVG, all of which target an Element; the target of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing
          event</a> is a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>.
        </p>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="sequence-of-events">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.6 </span>Sequence of events</h3>
        <p>
          The sequence in which <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing events</a> are queued is as follows:
        </p>
        <ol>
          <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingcancel">timingcancel</a> events are queued first.
              The sequence within <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingcancel">timingcancel</a> events is as follows:
              <ol>
                <li>
                  Events generated by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
                  associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> that was created earlier
                  precede events generated by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> associated
                  with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> created later.
                </li>
                <li>
                  Events generated by the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> are queued in the
                  order that the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-unattached-timed-item">unattached timed items</a> that generated
                  the events appear in the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-queue-of-unattached-timed-items">queue of
                  unattached timed items</a>
                  (see <a href="#event-dispatch-and-unattached-timed-items" class="sectionRef">section 5.7.4 Event dispatch and unattached timed items</a>).
                </li>
              </ol>
          </li>
          <li>All other events are ordered by <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</a> with
              earlier times preceding later times in the queue.</li>
          <li>For events with the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</a>, the following
              rules are applied in succession until the order in the queue is
              resolved,
            <ol>
              <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingstart">timingstart</a> events of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group" title="parent timing group">parents</a> precede all events
                  generated by <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item" title="child timed item">children</a>.</li>
              <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</a> events of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group" title="parent timing group">parents</a> precede all events
                  generated by <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item" title="child timed item">children</a> during
                  the iteration corresponding to the
                  <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</a> event's <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-iteration-index">event iteration
                  index</a>.</li>
              <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingend">timingend</a> events of <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group" title="parent timing group">parents</a> follow all events
                  generated by <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item" title="child timed item">children</a>.
                  <p class="note">
                    In effect, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item" title="child timed item">child timed items</a>
                    operate <em>inside</em> an iteration of their <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-parent-timing-group">parent
                    timing group</a> and hence events generated by children are
                    <em>wrapped</em> by their parents' events.
                  </p>
              </li>
              <li>For events generated by different <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
                  items</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingend">timingend</a> events precede <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingstart">timingstart</a>
                  events which precede <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</a> events.
                  <p class="note">
                    Note that sorting end events before start events is
                    consistent with the end-point exclusive nature of intervals
                    (see <a href="#interval-timing" class="sectionRef">section 3.8.4 Interval timing</a>).
                    When animation A ends at the same time as animation
                    B begins, we can imagine that animation A ends an infinitely
                    short amount of time before animation B begins such that
                    there is no overlap.
                  </p>
              </li>
              <li>For events generated by the same <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
                  items</a>, <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingstart">timingstart</a> events precede
                  <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingiteration">timingiteration</a> events which precede
                  <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingend">timingend</a> events.</li>
              <li>
                For events generated by <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed items</a>
                with a common <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>, events are
                ordered based on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-tree-order">tree order</a> traversal of the
                descendents of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-ancestor">ancestor</a> <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing group</a>.
              </li>
              <li>
                Events generated by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>
                associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> that was created earlier precede
                events generated by a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> associated with
                a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> created later.
              </li>
            </ol>
          </li>
        </ol>
      </div>
      <div class="section" id="event-dispatch">
        <h3><span class="secno">5.7 </span>Event dispatch</h3>
        <p>
          <dfn id="dfn-events-are-queued">Events are queued</dfn> when either of the following occurs:
        </p>
        <ul>
          <li>a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sampling" title="sampling">sampled</a>, or</li>
          <li>a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeking" title="seeking">seeked</a>.</li>
        </ul>
        <p>
          In the former case&#x2014;when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sampling" title="sampling">sampled</a>&#x2014;since Web Animations put no
          requirements on the time between successive samples, it is often the
          case  that the moment when a change in state that should produce an
          event is scheduled to occur does not line up with a sample.
        </p>
        <p>
          As such, except for the specific circumstances mentioned in following
          sections, the events that should be queued when <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sampling">sampling</a>
          a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> includes all events scheduled to occur in the
          interval since the previous sample time up to and including the
          current timeline time.
        </p>
        <p class="note">
          Note that when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is first <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-sampling" title="sampling">sampled</a>, it will employ <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event
          dispatch</a> as described in <a href="#event-dispatch-and-time-adjustments" class="sectionRef">section 5.7.3 Event dispatch and time adjustments</a>
          after which point the previous sample time for that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>
          will be resolved.
          As a result, there is never an occasion where the previous sample time
          is used and yet is undefined.
        </p>
        <p>
          For the latter case&#x2014;when a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeking" title="seeking">seeked</a>&#x2014;the behavior is defined in <a href="#event-dispatch-and-seeking-a-player" class="sectionRef">section 5.7.2 Event dispatch and seeking a player</a>.
        </p>
        <p class="todo">
          Make sure we update the previous sample time for a seek/etc.
        </p>
        <p class="note">
          Note that <a href="#algorithms-for-event-dispatch" class="sectionRef">section C. Algorithms for event dispatch</a> provides non-normative algorithms that
          incorporate the behavior defined in this section as well as <a href="#sequence-of-events" class="sectionRef">section 5.6 Sequence of events</a>.
        </p>
        <div class="section" id="seeked-event-dispatch">
          <h4><span class="secno">5.7.1 </span>Seeked event dispatch</h4>
          <div class="informative informative-bg">
            <p><em>This section is non-normative.</em></p><p>
              Under some circumstances the usual behavior of dispatching all
              events scheduled between two times is not appropriate either
              because it would produce such a large number of events that
              performance may be adversely affected,
              or because it would produce counter-intuitive results in the
              circumstances.
              In such situations, an alternative form of event dispatch called
              <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event dispatch</a> is used.
            </p>
          </div>
          <p>
            <dfn id="dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">Seeked event dispatch</dfn> is a mode of event dispatch that
            produces at most one <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-event">timing event</a> per <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> by
            comparing whether the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> was <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a> or not at
            some <var>initial moment</var> and at some <var>final moment</var>.
          </p>
          <p>
            To facilitate this, each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> has an associated
            <dfn id="dfn-previous-active-state">previous active state</dfn> property that initially has the
            value <em>inactive</em>.
          </p>
          <p>
            For a given <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> the events queued as a result of
            performing <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event dispatch</a> at <em>uneased local
            time</em> <var>t</var> is as follows:
          </p>
          <ol>
            <li>Let <var>timeline time</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> with which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is
                associated.
                The procedures for calculating the timeline time from a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
                item</a>'s <em>uneased local time</em> or the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current
                time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> are defined in <a href="#inverse-timing-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 5.3 Inverse timing calculations</a>.
                </li>
            <li>Let <var>iteration index</var> be the result of calculating the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-iteration">current iteration</a> at <var>t</var>.</li>
            <li>Let <var>timeline time</var> be the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-value">time value</a> of the
                <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timeline">timeline</a> with which the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is
                associated.
                The procedures for calculating the timeline time from a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
                item</a>'s <em>uneased local time</em> or the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-current-time">current
                time</a> of a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> are defined in <a href="#inverse-timing-calculations" class="sectionRef">section 5.3 Inverse timing calculations</a>.
                </li>
            <li>Let <var>current active state</var> be <em>active</em> if the
                timed item is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a> at <var>t</var>, and
                <em>inactive</em> otherwise.</li>
            <li>The events to be queued depend on comparing the <var>current
                active state</var> and the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-active-state">previous active
                state</a> as follows.
            <dl class="switch">
              <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-active-state">previous active state</a> is
                <em>active</em> and <var>current active state</var> is
                <em>inactive</em>,</dt>
              <dd>
                Queue a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingend">timingend</a> event with parameters:
                <ul>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-local-time">event local time</a>: <var>t</var></li>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</a>: <var>timeline time</var></li>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-iteration-index">event iteration index</a>: <var>iteration index</var>
                  </li><li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-dispatch-flag">seeked dispatch flag</a>: <var>true</var>
                </li></ul>
              </dd>
              <dt>If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-active-state">previous active state</a> is
                <em>inactive</em> and <var>current active state</var> is
                <em>active</em>,</dt>
              <dd>
                Queue a new <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingstart">timingstart</a> event with parameters:
                <ul>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-local-time">event local time</a>: <var>t</var></li>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-timeline-time">event timeline time</a>: <var>timeline time</var></li>
                  <li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-event-iteration-index">event iteration index</a>: <var>iteration index</var>
                  </li><li><a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-dispatch-flag">seeked dispatch flag</a>: <var>true</var>
                </li></ul>
              </dd>
            </dl>
            </li>
            <li>
              Let the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a>'s <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-active-state">previous active state</a> be
              <var>current active state</var>.
            </li>
          </ol>
          <p>
            For <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timing-group">timing groups</a>, this procedure is
            applied recursively to all <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-child-timed-item">child timed
            items</a>.
            The resulting events are sorted using the sequence defined in <a href="#sequence-of-events" class="sectionRef">section 5.6 Sequence of events</a>.
          </p>
          <p>
            Note that <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event dispatch</a> is only defined for <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed
            items</a> associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a>.
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">Timed items</a> not associated with a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> dispatch
            <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timingcancel">timingcancel</a> events as defined in <a href="#event-dispatch-and-time-adjustments" class="sectionRef">section 5.7.3 Event dispatch and time adjustments</a>.
          </p>
        </div>
        <div class="section" id="event-dispatch-and-seeking-a-player">
          <h4><span class="secno">5.7.2 </span>Event dispatch and seeking a player</h4>
          <p>
            When a seek is performed on a <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> (see <a href="#performing-a-seek" class="sectionRef">section 3.5.2.6 Performing a seek</a>) <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-seeked-event-dispatch">seeked event
            dispatch</a> is applied.
          </p>
          <p>
            Prior to performing the seek, the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-previous-active-state">previous active state</a> of
            each <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> that is either the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> of
            the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> or a descendent of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-source-content">source content</a> is
            updated to reflect whether the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-timed-item">timed item</a> is <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-active">active</a> or
            not at the moment prior to performing the seek.
          </p>
          <p>
            If the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-time-adjusted-flag">time adjusted flag</a> of the <a class="internalDFN" href="#dfn-player">player</a> has been set,
